Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-210 Termination of appointment of guardian -- General.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A guardian's authority and responsibility terminates upon the death, resignation, or removal of the guardian or upon the minor's death, adoption, marriage, or attainment of majority, but termination does not affect his liability for prior acts nor his obligation to account for funds and assets of his ward. Resignation of a guardian does not terminate the guardianship until it has been approved by the court. A testamentary appointment under an informally probated will terminates if the will is later denied probate in a formal proceeding.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-211 Proceedings subsequent to appointment -- Venue.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-211(1): The court where the ward resides has concurrent jurisdiction with the court which appointed the guardian, or in which acceptance of an appointment by will or written instrument was filed, over resignation, removal, accounting, and other proceedings relating to the guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-211(2): If the court located where the ward resides is not the court in which acceptance of appointment is filed, the court in which proceedings subsequent to appointment are commenced shall in all appropriate cases notify the other court, in this or another state, and after consultation with that court determine whether to retain jurisdiction or transfer the proceedings to the other court, whichever is in the best interest of the ward.  A copy of any order accepting a resignation or removing a guardian shall be sent to the court in which acceptance of appointment is filed.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-212 Resignation or removal proceedings.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-212(1): Any person interested in the welfare of a ward, or the ward, if 14 or more years of age, may petition for removal of a guardian on the ground that removal would be in the best interest of the ward. A guardian may petition for permission to resign. A petition for removal or for permission to resign may, but need not, include a request for appointment of a successor guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-212(2): After notice and hearing on a petition for removal or for permission to resign, the court may terminate the guardianship and make any further order that may be appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-212(3): If, at any time in the proceeding, the court determines that the interests of the ward are, or may be, inadequately represented, it may appoint an attorney to represent the minor, giving consideration to the preference of the minor if the minor is 14 or more years of age.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301 Appointment of guardian for incapacitated person.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301(1): 75-5-202.5 The parent of an incapacitated person may by will, or by written instrument as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301(2): The spouse of a married incapacitated person may by will or written instrument appoint a guardian of the incapacitated person.  The appointment becomes effective when, after having given seven days' prior written notice of his intention to do so to the incapacitated person and to the person having his care or with whom he resides or to at least one adult relative in the nearest degree of kinship to the incapacitated person in which there is an adult, the guardian files acceptance of appointment in the court in which the will is informally or formally probated or the written instrument is filed.  An effective appointment by a spouse has priority over an appointment by a parent unless it is terminated by the denial of probate in formal proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301(3): This state shall recognize a testamentary appointment effected by filing acceptance under a will probated at the testator's domicile in another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301(4): On the filing with the court in which the will was probated or the written instrument was filed, of written objection to the appointment by the person for whom a testamentary or instrumental appointment of guardian has been made, the appointment is terminated.  An objection does not prevent appointment by the court in a proper proceeding of the nominee named by will or written instrument or any other suitable person upon an adjudication of incapacity in proceedings under the succeeding sections of this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5 Rights of a person alleged to be incapacitated -- Rights of an incapacitated person.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(1): Except as otherwise provided by this chapter or any other law, a person alleged to be incapacitated has the right to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(1)(a): be represented by counsel before a guardianship is imposed and have counsel represent the person during the guardianship proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(1)(b): receive a copy of all documents filed in a guardianship proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(1)(c): have a relative, physician, physician assistant, or any interested person speak about or raise any issue of concern on behalf of the person during the guardianship proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(1)(d): receive information about guardianships from the court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(1)(e): be treated with respect and dignity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2): 75-5-312.5; 75-5-312; 75-5-417; 75-5-312; 75-5-417 Except as otherwise provided by this chapter or any other law, an incapacitated person for whom a guardian is appointed has right to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(a): have counsel represent the incapacitated person at any time after the guardian is appointed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(b): have a relative, physician, physician assistant, or any interested person speak about or raise any issue of concern on behalf of the person in any court hearing about the guardianship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(c): receive a copy of all documents filed in court regarding the guardianship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(d): receive information about guardianships from the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(e): ask questions and express concerns or complaints about a guardian and the actions of a guardian to the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(f): participate in developing an individualized plan for the incapacitated person's care, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(f)(i): managing the incapacitated person's assets and property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(f)(ii): determining the incapacitated person's residence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(f)(iii): determining the services to be received by the incapacitated person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(g): be given consideration in regards to the incapacitated person's current and previously stated desires, preferences for health care and medical treatment, and religious and moral beliefs;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(h): remain as independent as possible, including giving deference to the incapacitated person's preference for the incapacitated person's residence and standard of living:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(h)(i): as expressed or demonstrated before a determination of capacity was made; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(h)(ii): as currently expressed or demonstrated by the incapacitated person if the preference is reasonable under the circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(i): be granted the greatest degree of freedom possible that is consistent with the reasons for the guardianship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(j): be able to exercise control over all aspects of the incapacitated person's life that are not granted to the guardian in the order of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(k): engage in any activity that the court has not expressly reserved for the guardian, including marriage or domestic partnership, traveling, working, or having a driver license;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(l): be treated with respect and dignity;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(m): be treated fairly by the incapacitated person's guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(n): maintain privacy and confidentiality in personal matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(o): 75-5-312.5 receive telephone calls and personal mail and associate with relatives and acquaintances unless the guardian and the court determine that the association should be restricted or prohibited in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(p): receive timely, effective, and appropriate health care and medical treatment that does not violate the incapacitated person's rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(q): have all services provided by a guardian at a reasonable rate of compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(r): have a court review any request for payment by a guardian to avoid excessive or unnecessary fees or duplicative billing;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(s): receive prudent financial management of the incapacitated person's property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(t): 75-5-312; 75-5-417; 75-5-312; 75-5-417 subject to Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(u): receive and control the incapacitated person's salary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(v): maintain a bank account and manage the incapacitated person's personal money; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(w): ask the court to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(w)(i): review the management activity of a guardian if a dispute cannot be resolved regarding the guardian's management;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(w)(ii): continue to review the need for a guardianship or to modify or terminate a guardianship; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(2)(w)(iii): enter an order restoring the incapacitated person's capacity at the earliest possible time.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(3): The rights of an incapacitated person under this section do not abrogate any remedy provided by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(4): Any right described in this section may be:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(4)(a): addressed in a guardianship proceeding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-301.5(4)(b): enforced through a private cause of action.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-302 Venue.
-------------------------------------
The venue for guardianship proceedings for an incapacitated person is in the place where the incapacitated person resides or is present. If the incapacitated person is admitted to an institution pursuant to order of a court of competent jurisdiction, venue is also in the county in which that court sits.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303 Procedure for court appointment of a guardian of an incapacitated person.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(1): An incapacitated person or any person interested in the incapacitated person's welfare may petition for a finding of incapacity and appointment of a guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(2)(a): Upon the filing of a petition, the court shall set a date for hearing on the issues of incapacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(2)(b): Unless the allegedly incapacitated person has counsel of the person's own choice, the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the person in the proceeding the cost of which shall be paid by the person alleged to be incapacitated, unless the allegedly incapacitated person and the allegedly incapacitated person's parents are indigent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(2)(c): If the court determines that the petition is without merit, the attorney fees and court costs shall be paid by the person filing the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(2)(d): If the court appoints the petitioner or the petitioner's nominee as guardian of the incapacitated person, regardless of whether the nominee is specified in the moving petition or nominated during the proceedings, the petitioner shall be entitled to receive from the incapacitated person reasonable attorney fees and court costs incurred in bringing, prosecuting, or defending the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(3): The legal representation of the incapacitated person by an attorney shall terminate upon the appointment of a guardian, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(3)(a): there are separate conservatorship proceedings still pending before the court subsequent to the appointment of a guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(3)(b): there is a timely filed appeal of the appointment of the guardian or the determination of incapacity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(3)(c): upon an express finding of good cause, the court orders otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(4): The person alleged to be incapacitated may be examined by a physician or physician assistant appointed by the court who shall submit a report in writing to the court and may be interviewed by a visitor sent by the court.  The visitor also may interview the person seeking appointment as guardian, visit the present place of abode of the person alleged to be incapacitated and the place it is proposed that the person will be detained or reside if the requested appointment is made, conduct other investigations or observations as directed by the court, and submit a report in writing to the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5): 75-1-201; 75-3-1201
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(a): The person alleged to be incapacitated shall be present at the hearing in person and see or hear all evidence bearing upon the person's condition.  If the person seeking the guardianship requests a waiver of presence of the person alleged to be incapacitated, the court shall order an investigation by a court visitor, the costs of which shall be paid by the person seeking the guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(b): The investigation by a court visitor is not required if there is clear and convincing evidence from a physician that the person alleged to be incapacitated has:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(b)(i): fourth stage Alzheimer's Disease;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(b)(ii): extended comatosis; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(b)(iii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(b)(iii)(A): an intellectual disability; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(b)(iii)(B): an intelligence quotient score under 25.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(c): The person alleged to be incapacitated is entitled to be represented by counsel, to present evidence, to cross-examine witnesses, including the court-appointed physician and the visitor, and to trial by jury.  The issue may be determined at a closed hearing without a jury if the person alleged to be incapacitated or the person's counsel so requests.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d): 75-1-201; 75-3-1201 Counsel for the person alleged to be incapacitated, as defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(i): the person is the biological or adopted child of the petitioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(ii): 75-3-1201 the value of the person's entire estate does not exceed $20,000 as established by an affidavit of the petitioner in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(iii): the person appears in court with the petitioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(iv): the person is given the opportunity to communicate, to the extent possible, the person's acceptance of the appointment of petitioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(v): no attorney from the state court's list of attorneys who have volunteered to represent respondents in guardianship proceedings is able to provide counsel to the person within 60 days of the date of the appointment described in Subsection (2);
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(vi): the court is satisfied that counsel is not necessary in order to protect the interests of the person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-303(5)(d)(vii): the court appoints a visitor under Subsection (4).


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304 Findings -- Limited guardianship preferred -- Order of appointment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(1): The court may appoint a guardian as requested if the court is satisfied that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(1)(a): the person for whom a guardian is sought is incapacitated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(1)(b): the appointment is necessary or desirable as a means of providing continuing care and supervision of the incapacitated person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2)(a)(i): The court shall prefer a limited guardianship and may only grant a full guardianship if no other alternative exists.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2)(a)(ii): If the court does not grant a limited guardianship, a specific finding shall be made that nothing less than a full guardianship is adequate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2)(b)(i): An order of appointment of a limited guardianship shall state the limitations of the guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(2)(b)(ii): Letters of guardianship for a limited guardianship shall state the limitations of the guardianship unless the court determines for good cause shown that a limitation should not be listed in the letters.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(3): (3)(b); 75-5-301; 75-5-301(4)
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(3)(a): (3)(b); 75-5-301; 75-5-301(4) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(3)(b): Upon a finding that the testamentary or instrumental guardian has failed to accept the appointment within 30 days after notice of the guardianship proceeding, the court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(3)(b)(i): dismiss the proceeding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(3)(b)(ii): enter any other appropriate order.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-304(4): If the court grants a guardian with the power to make or assist with health care decisions for an incapacitated person, the court shall include in the order of appointment the name of any interested person for whom the guardian must notify of any significant health care or treatment received by the incapacitated person.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-305 Acceptance of appointment -- Consent to jurisdiction.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
By accepting appointment, a guardian submits personally to the jurisdiction of the court in any proceeding relating to the guardianship that may be instituted by any interested person or any person interested in the welfare of the ward. Notice of any proceeding shall be delivered to the guardian or mailed to him by ordinary mail at his address as listed in the court records and to his address as then known to the petitioner.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307 Removal or resignation of guardian.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(1)(b): make any other order that is appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2): 75-5-312; 75-5-312; 75-5-312.5 On a petition of removal of a guardian from the ward or any person interested in the ward's welfare, the court may remove a guardian if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(a): the guardian obtained the appointment by fraud, deceit, or gross misrepresentation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(b): 75-5-312 the guardian fails to perform the guardian's duties described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(c): 75-5-312 the guardian is unable to perform the guardian's duties, described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(d): the guardian fails to use reasonable care and diligence in the management of the ward's estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(e): 75-5-312.5 the guardian is found by the court to have filed a petition frivolously or in bad faith under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(f): the guardian's interests have become adverse to the faithful performance of the guardian's duties and there is a risk that the guardian will fail to faithfully perform the guardian's duties; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(2)(g): removal of the guardian would be in the best interest of the ward.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-307(5): The court is not required to appoint an attorney to represent the ward if the case is uncontested and the ward's incapacity is not at issue.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-308 Visitor in guardianship proceeding.
------------------------------------------------------------------
A visitor is, with respect to guardianship proceedings, a person who is trained in law, nursing, or social work and is an officer, employee, or special appointee of the court with no personal interest in the proceedings.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310 Emergency guardians.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310(1): If an incapacitated person has no guardian and an emergency exists or if an appointed guardian is not effectively performing the guardian's duties and the court further finds that the welfare of the incapacitated person requires immediate action, it may, without notice, appoint an emergency guardian for the person for a specified period not to exceed 30 days pending notice and hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310(2): 75-5-303 Upon request by an interested person after the appointment of an emergency guardian, the court shall hold a hearing within 14 days pursuant to Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5 Temporary guardians.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5(1): 75-5-303; 75-5-310; 75-5-310 If, after notice and hearing as required by Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5(1)(c): 75-5-310 appoint a different person as temporary guardian to replace an emergency guardian appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5(2): Unless the allegedly incapacitated person has already obtained counsel in this proceeding or an attorney has been already appointed for the person, the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the person in the proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5(3): Until a full hearing and further order of the court, the temporary guardian shall be charged with the care and custody of the ward and may not permit the ward to be removed from the state.  The authority of any permanent guardian previously appointed by the court is suspended so long as a temporary guardian has authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5(4): A temporary guardian may be removed at any time, and shall obey all orders and make any reports required by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-310.5(5): 75-5-312 A temporary guardian has all of the powers and duties of a permanent guardian as set forth in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(5)(a): all of the ward's estate received by the guardian in excess of those funds expended to meet current expenses for support, care, and education of the ward shall be paid to the conservator for management as provided in this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(5)(b): the guardian shall account to the conservator for funds expended.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(6)(a): Any guardian of a person for whom a conservator has been appointed:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(6)(a)(i): shall control the custody and care of the ward; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(6)(a)(ii): is entitled to receive reasonable sums for services and for room and board furnished to the ward as agreed upon between the guardian and the conservator if the amounts agreed upon are reasonable under the circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(6)(b): The guardian may request the conservator to expend the ward's estate by payment to third persons or institutions for the ward's care and maintenance.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(7): (7); (2)(k); (l)

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(7)(a)(i): makes a substantial misstatement on filings of annual reports;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312(7)(a)(ii): is guilty of gross impropriety in handling the property of the ward; or

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5 Association between an adult ward and a relative or acquaintance of the adult ward.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(a): "Associate" or "association" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(a)(i): visitation of an adult ward by a relative or qualified acquaintance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(a)(ii): communication between an adult ward and a relative or qualified acquaintance in any form, including by telephone, mail, or electronic communication.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(b): "Qualified acquaintance" means an individual, other than a relative of the adult ward, who:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(b)(i): has established a significant, mutual friendship with the adult ward; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(b)(ii): is clergy in the adult ward's religion or religious congregation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(1)(c): "Relative" means an adult ward's spouse, parent, step-parent, child, step-child, sibling, step-sibling, half-sibling, grandparent, grandchild, uncle, aunt, nephew, niece, or first cousin.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2)(a): Except as otherwise provided by court order, a guardian may not restrict or prohibit the right of an adult ward to associate with a relative or qualified acquaintance of the adult ward.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2)(b): If an adult ward is unable to express consent to visitation by a relative or a qualified acquaintance of the adult ward, the consent of the adult ward is presumed based on evidence of a prior relationship between the adult ward and the relative or qualified acquaintance of the adult ward.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2)(c): A guardian may not permit a relative or qualified acquaintance of an adult ward to associate with the adult ward:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2)(c)(i): if a court order prohibits the association;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2)(c)(ii): in a manner prohibited by court order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(2)(c)(iii): if the adult ward expresses a desire to not associate with the relative or qualified acquaintance.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(3): A guardian may, as part of the initial guardianship proceeding, petition the court to issue an order:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(3)(a): prohibiting or placing conditions on association between an adult ward and a relative or qualified acquaintance of the adult ward; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(3)(b): granting the guardian the authority to prohibit or place conditions on association between an adult ward and a relative or qualified acquaintance of the adult ward.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(4): (3); (3); (3); (3) A guardian may, at any time after the initial guardianship proceeding:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(4)(a): (3); (3) petition the court to issue an order described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(4)(b): (3); (3) petition, subject to notice, the court on an emergency basis to issue a temporary order until further order of the court described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(5): (3) An adult ward, a relative of an adult ward, or a qualified acquaintance of an adult ward may, at any time after the initial guardianship proceeding, petition the court to rescind or modify an order described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(6): (2) If a guardian violates Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(6)(a): file an ex parte motion to enforce an order or to obtain sanctions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(6)(b): seek an injunction to enforce compliance by the guardian with the law and any applicable court order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(6)(c): petition the court to have the guardian removed as guardian of the adult ward.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(7): For a hearing on a petition filed under this section, a court:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(7)(a): may appoint a court visitor to meet with the adult ward to determine the wishes of the adult ward regarding association;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(7)(b): shall give notice and an opportunity to be heard to the guardian, the adult ward, and the relative or qualified acquaintance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(7)(c): shall preserve the right of the adult ward to be present at the hearing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(7)(d): may order supervised visitation by the relative or qualified acquaintance before the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(8): A court may not enter an order prohibiting or placing restrictions on association between an adult ward and a relative or qualified acquaintance, unless the court finds by a preponderance of the evidence that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(8)(a): the adult ward desires the prohibition or restriction;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(8)(b): if the adult ward had the capacity to make a knowing and intelligent decision regarding the association, the adult ward would prohibit the association or impose the restriction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(8)(c): the prohibition or restriction is the least restrictive means necessary to protect the health or welfare of the adult ward.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(9): (8) In making the determination described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(9)(a): the wishes of the adult ward, expressed during or before the guardianship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(9)(b): the history of the relationship between the adult ward and the relative or qualified acquaintance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(9)(c): any history of criminal activity, abuse, neglect, or violence by the relative or qualified acquaintance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(9)(d): whether a protective order was ever issued against the relative or qualified acquaintance with respect to the adult ward.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(10): (11); (6)(a); (b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(10)(a): seeking an order prohibiting association or placing restrictions on association with a relative or qualified acquaintance of the adult ward;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(10)(b): modifying an order to place additional prohibitions or restrictions on association with a relative or qualified acquaintance of the adult ward; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(10)(c): (6)(a); (b) opposing an action described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(11): The relative or qualified acquaintance shall have the burden of proof if the relative or qualified acquaintance is seeking to modify an order previously entered by a court under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(12): (12)
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(12)(a): If, in a proceeding under this section, the court finds that the petition was filed frivolously or in bad faith, the court shall award attorney fees to a party opposing the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(12)(b): If, in a proceeding under this section, the court finds that the guardian is in contempt of court or has acted frivolously or in bad faith in prohibiting or restricting association, the court:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(12)(b)(i): shall award attorney fees to the prevailing party; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(12)(b)(ii): may impose a sanction, not to exceed $1,000, against the guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-312.5(12)(c): (12) A court shall prohibit attorney fees awarded under this Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-313 Proceedings subsequent to appointment -- Venue.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-313(1): The court where the ward resides has concurrent jurisdiction with the court which appointed the guardian or in which acceptance of an appointment by will or written instrument was filed over resignation, removal, accounting, and other proceedings relating to the guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-313(2): If the court located where the ward resides is not the court in which acceptance of appointment is filed, the court in which proceedings subsequent to appointment are commenced shall in all appropriate cases notify the other court, in this or another state, and after consultation with that court determine whether to retain jurisdiction or transfer the proceedings to the other court, whichever may be in the best interest of the ward.  A copy of any order accepting a resignation or removing a guardian shall be sent to the court in which acceptance of appointment is filed.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-314 Mentally incompetent veteran -- Evidence of necessity for appointment of guardian.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Where a petition is filed for the appointment of a guardian for a mentally incompetent ward, a certificate of the administrator or his duly authorized representative, that such person has been rated incompetent by the veterans administration on examination in accordance with the laws and regulations governing such veterans administration and that the appointment of a guardian is a condition precedent to the payment of any money due such ward by the veterans administration, shall be prima facie evidence of the necessity for such appointment.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-315 Copies of public records furnished to veterans administration.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
When a copy of any public record is required by the veterans administration to be used in determining the eligibility of any person to participate in benefits made available by the veterans administration, the official custodian of such public record shall without charge provide the applicant for such benefits or any person acting on behalf of the authorized representative of the veterans administration with a certified copy of such record.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316 Expedited guardianship proceedings.
------------------------------------------------------------------
The court finds that:Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(1)(a): With regard to persons who are residents of the Utah State Developmental Center, the expedited process provided by this section may be applied to obtain a limited guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(1)(b): For purposes of this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(1)(b)(i): "Limited guardianship" means a guardianship solely for the purpose of granting consent for medical care and for participation in approval of the ward's individualized program plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(1)(b)(ii): "Ward" means a resident of the Utah State Developmental Center who is the subject of guardianship proceedings under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(2): Any person interested in the incapacitated person's welfare may file a petition for a finding of incapacity and appointment of a guardian.  That person may seek the limited guardianship pro se, using the forms described in this section.  Any fee for filing a petition for a limited guardianship shall be waived if the guardian is proceeding under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(3): Upon filing a petition for limited guardianship under this section, the court shall set a date for hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(4): The ward has the right to be present at the hearing and to see and hear all evidence relating to his condition.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(5): (11); (6) At that hearing the court shall review the affidavit of the superintendent of the Utah State Developmental Center, described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(6): If the proposed guardian is not a parent or relative of the ward, personal notice shall be given to the ward's spouse, parents, and any adult children of the ward.  Personal notice shall also be given to other persons as the court may direct.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(7): The court may, in its discretion, appoint a guardian ad litem to represent the ward in the hearing, and may request independent evaluation by a physician appointed by the court.  The physician shall submit his findings to the court in writing.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(8): The court may grant the petition for a limited guardianship and sign the Order of Appointment if the court finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(8)(a): the appropriate parties have been given notice;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(8)(b): the ward is incapacitated, based on the affidavit of the superintendent of the Utah State Developmental Center and any affidavit or testimony of persons entitled to receive notice or requested to present evidence under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(8)(c): it is necessary and desirable to establish the guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(9): 75-5-302 Venue for these expedited guardianship proceedings shall be the same as that described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(10): A petition for a limited guardianship shall include the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(10)(a): the interest of the petitioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(10)(b): the name, age, residence, and address of the ward;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(10)(c): verification that the ward is a resident of the Utah State Developmental Center;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(10)(d): the name and address of the nearest relative of the ward; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(10)(e): the reason for appointment of guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11): The petitioner shall also provide the court with an affidavit of the superintendent of the Utah State Developmental Center that includes the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11)(a): that the ward is a resident of the Utah State Developmental Center;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11)(b): the date the ward was originally admitted to the Utah State Developmental Center;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11)(c): the diagnosis of the ward, including a description of the ward's disabling condition, the level of the ward's intellectual disability, and any medical or physical conditions of the ward;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11)(d): that the Utah State Developmental Center is certified as an intermediate care facility for people with an intellectual disability;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11)(e): that because of that certification, the Utah State Developmental Center receives financial participation from the United States Government for its operation and maintenance costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(11)(f): that federal regulations under Title XIX require the ward to have a guardian appointed for the sole purpose of giving consent for medical and dental care and of participation in and approval of the ward's individual program plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12): If the court finds that, under the requirements of this section the proposed limited guardian should be appointed, it shall enter an order establishing that limited guardianship in substantially the following form:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12)(a): appointment of a limited guardianship for (named ward) is necessary and desirable as a means of providing continuing care and supervision and to ensure his welfare;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12)(b): the ward is incapacitated;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12)(c): (named guardian) is appointed as the limited guardian of (named ward); and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12)(d): the guardianship is a limited guardianship solely for the purpose of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12)(d)(i): granting permission for medical and dental care on behalf of the ward; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(12)(d)(ii): participation in the development and approval of the ward's individual program plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-316(13): Appointment of guardianship under this section places no additional responsibility or liability on the guardian with regard to the ward.  The limited guardianship is solely for consent for medical care and approval of the ward's individualized program plan, and shall not be construed to increase or create liability or responsibility for the guardian.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401 Protective proceedings.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(1): (1)(a) Upon petition and after notice and hearing in accordance with the provisions of this part, the court may appoint a conservator or make other protective order for cause as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(1)(a): Appointment of a conservator or other protective order may be made in relation to the estate and affairs of a minor if the court determines that a minor owns money or property that requires management or protection which cannot otherwise be provided, has or may have business affairs which may be jeopardized or prevented by minority, or that funds are needed for the minor's support and education and protection is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(1)(b): (1)(a) The provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(2): Appointment of a conservator or other protective order may be made in relation to the estate and affairs of a person if the court determines that the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(2)(a): is unable to manage the person's property and affairs effectively for reasons such as mental illness, mental deficiency, physical illness or disability, chronic use of drugs, chronic intoxication, confinement, detention by a foreign power, or disappearance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(2)(b): has property which will be wasted or dissipated unless proper management is provided or that funds are needed for the support, care, and welfare of the person or those entitled to be supported by the person and protection is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-401(3): Appointment of a conservator or other protective order may not be denied solely on the basis that the person for whom the conservatorship or other protective order is sought has a valid power of attorney in effect.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-402 Protective proceedings -- Jurisdiction of affairs of protected persons.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
After the service of notice in a proceeding seeking the appointment of a conservator or other protective order and until termination of the proceeding, the court in which the petition is filed has:Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-402(1): Exclusive jurisdiction to determine the need for a conservator or other protective order until the proceedings are terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-402(2): Exclusive jurisdiction to determine how the estate of the protected person which is subject to the laws of this state shall be managed, expended, or distributed to or for the use of the protected person or any of his dependents;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-402(3): Concurrent jurisdiction to determine the validity of claims against the person or estate of the protected person and his title to any property or claim.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-403 Venue.
-------------------------------------
Venue for proceedings under this part is:Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-403(1): In the county in this state where the person to be protected resides, whether or not a guardian has been appointed in another place; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-403(2): If the person to be protected does not reside in this state, in any county where he has property.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-404 Original petition for appointment or protective order.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-404(1): The person to be protected, any person who is interested in his estate, affairs, or welfare, including his parent, guardian, or custodian, or any person who would be adversely affected by lack of effective management of his property and affairs may petition for the appointment of a conservator or for other appropriate protective order.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-404(2): The petition shall set forth to the extent known, the interest of the petitioner; the name, age, residence, and address of the person to be protected; the name and address of his guardian, if any; the name and address of his nearest relative known to the petitioner; a general statement of his property with an estimate of the value thereof, including any compensation, insurance, pension, or allowance to which he is entitled; and the reason why appointment of a conservator or other protective order is necessary. If the appointment of a conservator is requested, the petition also shall set forth the name and address of the person whose appointment is sought and the basis of his priority for appointment.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-405 Notice.
--------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-405(1): 75-1-401 On a petition for appointment of a conservator or other protective order, the person to be protected and his spouse or, if none, his parents, must be served personally with notice of the proceeding at least 10 days before the date of the hearing if they can be found within the state, or, if they cannot be found within the state, they must be given notice in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-405(2): 75-5-406; (1); 75-1-401 Notice of a petition for appointment of a conservator or other initial protective order, and of any subsequent hearing, must be given to any person who has filed a request for notice under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-406 Protective proceedings -- Request for notice -- Interested person.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any interested person who desires to be notified before any order is made in a protective proceeding may file with the registrar a request for notice subsequent to payment of any fee required by statute or court rule. The clerk shall mail a copy of the demand to the conservator if one has been appointed. A request is not effective unless it contains a statement showing the interest of the person making it and his address, or that of his attorney, and is effective only as to matters occurring after the filing. Any governmental agency paying or planning to pay benefits to the person to be protected is an interested person in protective proceedings.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407 Procedure concerning hearing and order on original petition.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(1): Upon receipt of a petition for appointment of a conservator or other protective order because of minority, the court shall set a date for the hearing on the matters alleged in the petition.  If, at any time in the proceeding, the court determines that the interests of the minor are or may be inadequately represented, it may appoint an attorney to represent the minor, giving consideration to the choice of the minor if 14 years of age or older.  An attorney appointed by the court to represent a minor has the powers and duties of a guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(2): Upon receipt of a petition for appointment of a conservator or other protective order for reasons other than minority, the court shall set a date for hearing.  Unless the person to be protected has already retained counsel, the court may appoint an attorney to represent the person to be protected who then has the powers and duties of a guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(3): The legal representation of the protected person by an attorney shall terminate upon the appointment of a conservator, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(3)(a): there are separate guardianship proceedings still pending before the court subsequent to the appointment of a conservator;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(3)(b): there is a timely filed appeal of the appointment of the conservator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(3)(c): upon an express finding of good cause, the court orders otherwise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(4): If the alleged disability is mental illness, mental deficiency, physical illness or disability, advanced age, chronic use of drugs, or chronic intoxication, the court may direct that the person to be protected be examined by a physician designated by the court, preferably a physician who is not connected with any institution in which the person is a patient or is detained.  The court may send a visitor to interview the person to be protected.  The visitor may be a guardian ad litem or an officer or employee of the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-407(5): After hearing, upon finding that a basis for the appointment of a conservator or other protective order has been established, the court shall make an appointment or other appropriate protective order.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408 Permissible court orders.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1): The court has the following powers which may be exercised directly or through a conservator in respect to the estate and affairs of protected persons:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(a): While a petition for appointment of a conservator or other protective order is pending and after preliminary hearing and without notice to others, the court has power to preserve and apply the property of the person to be protected as may be required for the person's benefit or the benefit of the person's dependents.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(b): After hearing and upon determining that a basis for an appointment or other protective order exists with respect to a minor without other disability, the court has all those powers over the estate and affairs of the minor which are or might be necessary for the best interests of the minor, the minor's family, and the members of the minor's household.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c): After hearing and upon determining that a basis for an appointment or other protective order exists with respect to a person for reasons other than minority, the court has, for the benefit of the person and members of the person's household, all the powers over the person's estate and affairs that the person could exercise if present and not under disability, except the power to make a will.  These powers include the power to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(i): make gifts;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(ii): convey or release the person's contingent and expectant interests in property including marital property rights and any right of survivorship incident to joint tenancy or tenancy by the entirety;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(iii): exercise or release the person's powers as personal representative, custodian for minors, conservator, or donee of a power of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(iv): enter into contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(v): create revocable or irrevocable trusts of property of the estate that may extend beyond the person's disability or life;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(vi): exercise options of the person with a disability to purchase securities or other property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(vii): exercise the person's rights to elect options and change beneficiaries under insurance and annuity policies and to surrender the policies for their cash value;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(viii): exercise the person's right to an elective share in the estate of the person's deceased spouse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(c)(ix): renounce any interest by testate or intestate succession or by inter vivos transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(1)(d): The court may exercise, or direct the exercise of, its authority to exercise or release powers of appointment of which the protected person is donee, to renounce interests, to make gifts in trust or otherwise exceeding 20% of any year's income of the estate, or to change beneficiaries under insurance and annuity policies, only if satisfied, after notice and hearing, that it is in the best interests of the protected person, and that the person either is incapable of consenting or has consented to the proposed exercise of power.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(2): An order made pursuant to this section determining that a basis for appointment of a conservator or other protective order exists has no effect on the capacity of the protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-408(3): (1); 75-5-417; 75-5-418; 75-5-419; 75-5-424 If the court elects to appoint a conservator under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-409 Protective arrangements and single transactions authorized.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-409(1): 75-5-401 If it is established in a proper proceeding that a basis exists as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-409(2): 75-5-401 When it has been established in a proper proceeding that a basis exists as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-409(3): Before approving a protective arrangement or other transaction under this section, the court shall consider the interests of creditors and dependents of the protected person and, in view of his disability, whether the protected person needs the continuing protection of a conservator. The court may appoint a special conservator to assist in the accomplishment of any protective arrangement or other transaction authorized under this section who shall have the authority conferred by the order and serve until discharged by order after report to the court of all matters done pursuant to the order of appointment.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410 Who may be appointed conservator -- Priorities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
I, (Name), being of sound mind and not acting under duress, fraud, or other undue influence, do hereby nominate (Name, current residence, and relationship, if any, of the nominee) to serve as the conservator of my property in the event that after the date of this instrument I become incapacitated or have other need for protection.Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1): (1)(c) The court may appoint an individual, or a corporation with general power to serve as trustee, as conservator of the estate of a protected person.  The following are entitled to consideration for appointment in the order listed:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(a): a conservator, guardian of property, or other like fiduciary appointed or recognized by the appropriate court of any other jurisdiction in which the protected person resides;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(b): an individual or corporation nominated by the protected person if he is 14 or more years of age and has, in the opinion of the court, sufficient mental capacity to make an intelligent choice;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(c): the court shall appoint a conservator in accordance with the protected person's most recent nomination, unless the potential conservator is disqualified or the court finds other good cause why that person should not serve as conservator.  The nomination shall be in writing and shall be signed by the person making the nomination.  The nomination shall be in substantially the following form:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(d): (1)(c) a person who has been nominated by the protected person, by any means other than that described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(e): the spouse of the protected person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(f): an adult child of the protected person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(g): a parent of the protected person, or a person nominated by the will of a deceased parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(h): any relative of the protected person with whom he has resided for more than six months prior to the filing of the petition;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(1)(i): a person nominated by the person who is caring for him or paying benefits to him.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-410(2): (1)(a); (e); (f); (g); (h) A person in the priorities described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-411 Bond.
------------------------------------
Subject to the provisions of

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412 Terms and requirements of bonds.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412(1): 75-5-411 The following requirements and provisions apply to any bond required under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412(1)(a): Unless otherwise provided by the terms of the approved bond, sureties are jointly and severally liable with the conservator and with each other;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412(1)(b): By executing an approved bond of a conservator, the surety consents to the jurisdiction of the court which issued letters to the primary obligor in any proceeding pertaining to the fiduciary duties of the conservator and naming the surety as a party defendant. Notice of the proceeding shall be delivered to the surety or mailed to him by registered or certified mail at his address as listed with the court where the bond is filed and to his address as then known to the petitioner;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412(1)(c): On petition of a successor conservator or any interested person, a proceeding may be initiated against a surety for breach of the obligation of the bond of the conservator;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412(1)(d): The bond of the conservator is not void after the first recovery but may be proceeded against from time to time until the whole penalty is exhausted.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-412(2): No proceeding may be commenced against the surety on any matter as to which an action or proceeding against the primary obligor is barred by adjudication or limitation under this code.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-413 Acceptance of appointment -- Consent to jurisdiction.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
By accepting appointment, a conservator submits personally to the jurisdiction of the court in any proceeding relating to the estate that may be instituted by any interested person. Notice of any proceeding shall be delivered to the conservator or mailed to him by registered or certified mail at his address as listed in the petition for appointment, or as thereafter reported to the court, and to his address as then known to the petitioner.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-414 Compensation and expenses.
---------------------------------------------------------
If not otherwise compensated for services rendered, any visitor, lawyer, physician, conservator, or special conservator appointed in a protective proceeding is entitled to reasonable compensation from the estate.  If the court appoints the petitioner or the petitioner's nominee as conservator over the protected person, regardless of whether the nominee is specified in the moving petition or nominated during the proceedings, the petitioner is entitled to receive from the estate reasonable attorney fees and court costs incurred in bringing and defending the petition.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-415 Death, resignation, or removal of conservator.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-415(1): The court may remove a conservator for good cause, upon notice and hearing, or accept the resignation of a conservator.  After the death, resignation, or removal of a conservator, the court may appoint another conservator.  A conservator so appointed succeeds to the title and powers of the preceding conservator.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-415(2): 75-5-407 Before removing a conservator, accepting the resignation of a conservator, or ordering that a protected person's incapacity has terminated, the court shall follow the same procedures to safeguard the rights of the protected person as apply to a petition for appointment of a conservator as provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416 Petitions for orders subsequent to appointment.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(1): Title 75, Chapter 7, Utah Uniform Trust Code Any person interested in the welfare of a person for whom a conservator has been appointed may file a petition in the appointing court for an order:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(1)(a): requiring bond or security or additional bond or security, or reducing bond;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(1)(b): requiring an accounting for the administration of the conservatorship estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(1)(c): directing distribution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(1)(d): removing the conservator and appointing a temporary or successor conservator; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(1)(e): Title 75, Chapter 7, Utah Uniform Trust Code granting other appropriate relief, including any relief available under
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(2): A conservator may petition the appointing court for instructions concerning the conservator's fiduciary responsibility.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-416(3): Upon notice and hearing the court may give appropriate instructions or make any appropriate order.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-417 General duty of conservator.
-----------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418 Inventory and records.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418(1): Within 90 days after appointment of a conservator, the conservator shall prepare and file with the appointing court a complete inventory of the estate of the protected person together with an oath or affirmation that it is complete and accurate so far as the conservator is informed.  The estate of the protected person does not include the assets of a trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418(2): The conservator shall provide a copy of the inventory to the protected person if the person:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418(2)(a): can be located;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418(2)(b): has attained the age of 14 years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418(2)(c): has sufficient mental capacity to understand these matters, and to any parent or guardian with whom the protected person resides.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-418(3): The conservator shall keep suitable financial records and produce them upon the request of any interested person.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-419 Accounts.
----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-419(1): Every conservator must account to the court for the administration of the estate upon resignation or removal and at any other times the court may direct.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-419(2): On termination of the protected person's minority or disability, a conservator may account to the court, the former protected person, or the personal representative of the protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-419(3): Subject to appeal or vacation within the time permitted, an order, made upon notice and hearing, allowing an intermediate account of a conservator, adjudicates as to any liabilities concerning the matters considered in connection with the protected person's account, and an order, made upon notice and hearing, allowing a final account adjudicates as to all previously unsettled liabilities of the conservator to the protected person or the protected person's successors relating to the conservatorship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-419(4): In connection with any account, the court may require a conservator to submit to a physical check of the estate in the conservator's control, to be made in any manner the court may specify.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-420 Conservators -- Title by appointment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-420(1): The appointment of a conservator vests in the conservator title as fiduciary to all property of the protected person, presently held or thereafter acquired, not including the assets of a trust, including title to any property previously held for the protected person by custodians or attorneys-in-fact, except for property held pursuant to any uniform gifts to minors act or provisions.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-420(2): The appointment of a conservator is not a transfer or alienation within the meaning of general provisions of any federal or state statute or regulation, insurance policy, pension plan, contract, will, or trust instrument imposing restrictions upon or penalties for transfer or alienation by the protected person of any rights or interest, but this section does not restrict the ability of persons to make specific provision by contract or dispositive instrument relating to a conservator.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-421 Recording of conservator's letters.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-421(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-421(1)(a): Letters of conservatorship are evidence of transfer of the assets of a protected person to the conservator.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-421(1)(b): An order terminating a conservatorship is evidence of transfer of the assets of the estate from the conservator to the protected person or the protected person's successors.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-421(1)(c): Subject to the requirements of general statutes governing the filing or recordation of documents of title to land or other property, letters of conservatorship and orders terminating conservatorships may be filed or recorded to give record notice of title as between the conservator and the protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-421(2): A person who refuses to accept the authority of a conservator to transact business with the assets of the protected person after receiving a certified copy of letters of conservatorship is liable for costs, expenses, attorney fees, and damages if the court determines that the person did not act in good faith in refusing to accept the authority of the conservator.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-422 Sale, encumbrance or transaction involving conflict of interest -- Voidable -- Exceptions.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any sale or encumbrance to a conservator, his spouse, agent, or attorney, or any corporation or trust in which he has a substantial beneficial interest, or any transaction which is affected by a substantial conflict of interest, is voidable unless the transaction is approved by the court after notice to interested persons and others as directed by the court.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-423 Persons dealing with conservators -- Protection.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person who in good faith either assists a conservator or deals with him for value in any transaction, other than those requiring a court order as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424 Powers of conservator in administration.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(1): 75-5-209; Part 2, Guardians of Minors A conservator has all of the powers conferred in this chapter and any additional powers conferred by law on trustees in this state.  In addition, a conservator of the estate of an unmarried minor as to whom no one has parental rights, has the duties and powers of a guardian of a minor described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(2)(a): A conservator has the power to compel the production of the protected person's estate documents, including the protected person's will, trust, power of attorney, and any advance health care directives.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(2)(b): If a guardian is also appointed for the ward, the conservator shall share with the guardian the estate documents the conservator receives.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(3): A conservator has power without court authorization or confirmation to invest and reinvest funds of the estate as would a trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4): (3); (4)(w)(i) A conservator, acting reasonably in efforts to accomplish the purpose for which the conservator was appointed, may use the funds of the estate and act without court authorization or confirmation, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(a): collect, hold, and retain assets of the estate, including land in another state, until, in the conservator's judgment, disposition of the assets should be made, and the assets may be retained even though they include an asset in which the conservator is personally interested;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(b): receive additions to the estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(c): continue or participate in the operation of any business or other enterprise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(d): acquire an undivided interest in an estate asset in which the conservator, in any fiduciary capacity, holds an undivided interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(e): (3) invest and reinvest estate assets in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(f): deposit estate funds in a bank including a bank operated by the conservator;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(g): acquire or dispose of an estate asset, including land in another state, for cash or on credit, at public or private sale; and to manage, develop, improve, exchange, partition, change the character of, or abandon an estate asset;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(h): make ordinary or extraordinary repairs or alterations in buildings or other structures, demolish any improvements, and raze existing or erect new party walls or buildings;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(i):

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(i)(ii): make or obtain the vacation of plats and adjust boundaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(i)(iii): adjust differences in valuation on exchange or partition by giving or receiving considerations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(i)(iv): dedicate easements to public use without consideration;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(j): enter for any purpose into a lease as lessor or lessee with or without option to purchase or renew for a term within or extending beyond the term of the conservatorship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(k): enter into a lease or arrangement for exploration and removal of minerals or other natural resources or enter into a pooling or unitization agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(l): grant an option involving disposition of an estate asset or take an option for the acquisition of any asset;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(m): vote a security, in person or by general or limited proxy;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(n): pay calls, assessments, and any other sums chargeable or accruing against or on account of securities;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(o): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(o)(i): sell or exercise stock subscription or conversion rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(o)(ii): consent, directly or through a committee or other agent, to the reorganization, consolidation, merger, dissolution, or liquidation of a corporation or other business enterprise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(p): hold a security in the name of a nominee or in other form without disclosure of the conservatorship so that title to the security may pass by delivery, but the conservator is liable for any act of the nominee in connection with the stock so held;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(q): insure the assets of the estate against damage or loss and the conservator against liability with respect to third persons;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(r): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(r)(i): borrow money to be repaid from estate assets or otherwise; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(r)(ii): advance money for the protection of the estate or the protected person, and for all expenses, losses, and liabilities sustained in the administration of the estate or because of the holding or ownership of any estate assets, and the conservator has a lien on the estate as against the protected person for advances so made;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(s): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(s)(i): pay or contest any claim;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(s)(ii): settle a claim by or against the estate or the protected person by compromise, arbitration, or otherwise; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(s)(iii): release, in whole or in part, any claim belonging to the estate to the extent that the claim is uncollectible;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(t): pay taxes, assessments, compensation of the conservator, and other expenses incurred in the collection, care, administration, and protection of the estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(u): allocate items of income or expense to either estate income or principal, as provided by law, including creation of reserves out of income for depreciation, obsolescence, or amortization, or for depletion in mineral or timber properties;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(v): pay any sum distributable to a protected person or dependent without liability to the conservator, by paying the sum to the distributee or by paying the sum for the use of the distributee either to the distributee's guardian, or if none, to a relative or other person with custody of the person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(w): (4)(w)(i)
