Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(w)(iii): instead of acting personally, employ one or more agents to perform any act of administration, whether or not discretionary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(x): prosecute or defend actions, claims, or proceedings in any jurisdiction for the protection of estate assets and of the conservator in the performance of the conservator's duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(y): act as a qualified beneficiary of any trust in which the protected person is a qualified beneficiary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-424(4)(z): execute and deliver the instruments that will accomplish or facilitate the exercise of the powers vested in the conservator.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425 Distributive duties and powers of conservator.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1): (1) A conservator may expend or distribute income or principal of the estate without court authorization or confirmation for the support, education, care, or benefit of the protected person and the protected person's dependents in accordance with the following principles:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(a): The conservator is to consider recommendations relating to the appropriate standard of support, education, and benefit for the protected person made by a parent or guardian, if any. A conservator may not be surcharged for sums paid to persons or organizations actually furnishing support, education, or care to the protected person pursuant to the recommendations of a parent or guardian of the protected person unless the conservator knows that the parent or guardian is deriving personal financial benefit therefrom, including relief from any personal duty of support, or unless the recommendations are clearly not in the best interests of the protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(b): The conservator is to expend or distribute sums reasonably necessary for the support, education, care or benefit of the protected person with due regard to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(b)(i): the size of the estate, the probable duration of the conservatorship and the likelihood that the protected person, at some future time, may be fully able to manage the protected person's affairs and the estate which has been conserved for the protected person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(b)(ii): the accustomed standard of living of the protected person and members of the protected person's household; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(b)(iii): other funds or sources used for the support of the protected person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(c): The conservator may expend funds of the estate for the support of persons legally dependent on the protected person and others who are members of the protected person's household who are unable to support themselves and who are in need of support.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(1)(d): (1) Funds expended under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(2): (1) If the estate is ample to provide for the purposes implicit in the distributions authorized by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(3): 75-5-401(2)(a) When a person who is a minor and who has not been adjudged to have a disability under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(4): When the conservator is satisfied that a protected person's disability, other than minority, has ceased, the conservator, after meeting all prior claims and expenses of administration, shall pay over and distribute all funds and properties to the former protected person as soon as possible.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5): If a protected person dies, the conservator:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5)(a): shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5)(a)(i): deliver to the court for safekeeping any will of the deceased protected person that may have come into the conservator's possession;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5)(a)(ii): inform the personal representative or a beneficiary named in the will that the conservator has done so; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5)(a)(iii): retain the estate for delivery to a duly appointed personal representative of the decedent or other persons entitled to it;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5)(b): may continue to pay the obligations lawfully due against the estate and to protect the estate from waste, injury, or damages that might reasonably be foreseeable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(5)(c): may apply to exercise the powers and duties of a personal representative so that the conservator may proceed to administer and distribute the decedent's estate without additional or further appointment, provided that at least 40 days from the death of the protected person no other person has been appointed personal representative and no application or petition for appointment is before the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-425(6): (5)(c); 75-3-310; 75-3-308; Chapter 3, Part 6, Personal Representative - Appointment, Control, and Termination of Authority; Part 7, Duties and Powers of Personal Representatives; Part 8, Creditors' Claims; Part 9, Special Provisions Relating to Distribution; Part 10, Closing Estates Upon application for an order granting the powers of a personal representative to a conservator as provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-426 Enlargement or limitation of powers of conservator.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Subject to the restrictions of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-427 Preservation of estate plan.
-----------------------------------------------------------
In investing the estate, and in selecting assets of the estate for distribution under Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428 Claims against protected person -- Enforcement.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428(1): A conservator must pay from the estate all just claims against the estate and against the protected person arising before or after the conservatorship upon their presentation and allowance.  A claim may be presented by either of the following methods:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428(1)(a): The claimant may deliver or mail to the conservator a written statement of the claim indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant, and the amount claimed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428(1)(b): The claimant may file a written statement of the claim, in the form prescribed by rule, with the clerk of the court and deliver or mail a copy of the statement to the conservator.  A claim is considered presented on the first to occur of receipt of the written statement of claim by the conservator, or the filing of the claim with the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428(2): A presented claim is allowed if it is not disallowed by written statement mailed by the conservator to the claimant within 60 days after its presentation.  The presentation of a claim tolls any statute of limitation relating to the claim until 30 days after its disallowance.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428(3): A claimant whose claim has not been paid may petition the court for determination of his claim at any time before it is barred by the applicable statute of limitation, and, upon due proof, procure an order for its allowance and payment from the estate.  If a proceeding is pending against a protected person at the time of appointment of a conservator or is initiated against the protected person thereafter, the moving party must give notice of the proceeding to the conservator if the outcome is to constitute a claim against the estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-428(4): If it appears that the estate in conservatorship is likely to be exhausted before all existing claims are paid, preference is to be given to prior claims for the care, maintenance, and education of the protected person or his dependents and existing claims for expenses of administration.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-429 Individual liability of conservator.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-429(1): Unless otherwise provided in the contract, a conservator is not individually liable on a contract properly entered into in his fiduciary capacity in the course of administration of the estate unless he fails to reveal his representative capacity and identify the estate in the contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-429(2): The conservator is individually liable for obligations arising from ownership or control of property of the estate or for torts committed in the course of administration of the estate only if he is personally at fault.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-429(3): Claims based on contracts entered into by a conservator in his fiduciary capacity, on obligations arising from ownership or control of the estate, or on torts committed in the course of administration of the estate may be asserted against the estate by proceeding against the conservator in his fiduciary capacity, whether or not the conservator is individually liable therefor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-429(4): Any question of liability between the estate and the conservator individually may be determined in a proceeding for accounting, surcharge, indemnification, or other appropriate proceeding or action.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-430 Termination of proceeding.
---------------------------------------------------------
The protected person, his personal representative, the conservator, or any other interested person may petition the court to terminate the conservatorship. A protected person seeking termination is entitled to the same rights and procedures as in an original proceeding for a protective order. The court, upon determining after notice and hearing that the minority or disability of the protected person has ceased, may terminate the conservatorship. Upon termination, title to assets of the estate passes to the former protected person or to his successors, subject to provision in the order for expenses of administration or to conveyances from the conservator to the former protected persons or his successors to evidence the transfer.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-431 Payment of debt and delivery of property to foreign conservator without local proceedings.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-431(1): Any person indebted to a protected person, or having possession of property or of an instrument evidencing a debt, stock, or chose in action belonging to a protected person, may pay or deliver to a conservator, guardian of the estate, or other like fiduciary appointed by a court of the state of residence of the protected person, upon being presented with proof of his appointment and an affidavit made by him or on his behalf stating:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-431(1)(a): That no protective proceeding relating to the protected person is pending in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-431(1)(b): That the foreign conservator is entitled to payment or to receive delivery.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-431(2): If the person to whom the affidavit is presented is not aware of any protective proceeding pending in this state, payment or delivery in response to the demand and affidavit discharges the debtor or possessor.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-432 Foreign conservator -- Proof of authority -- Bond -- Powers.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If no local conservator has been appointed and no petition in a protective proceeding is pending in this state, a domiciliary foreign conservator may file with a court in this state in a county in which property belonging to the protected person is located, authenticated copies of his appointment and of any official bond he has given. Thereafter, he may exercise as to assets in this state all powers of a local conservator and may maintain actions and proceedings in this state subject to any conditions imposed upon nonresident parties generally.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5-433 Embezzlement of protected person's estate -- Citation to person suspected.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Upon petition made by any interested person against anyone suspected of having concealed, embezzled, or conveyed away any of the money, goods or effects, or an instrument in writing, belonging to the protected person, ward, or to his estate, the court may cite the suspected person to appear before it and may examine and proceed with him on the charge; and if on such examination it appears that he has wrongful possession of any such property, the court may order the delivery of the same to the conservator or guardian.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 75 - Chapter 5b - Uniform Adult Guardianship and Protective Proceedings Jurisdiction Act
********************************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Uniform Adult Guardianship and Protective Proceedings Jurisdiction Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
In this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(1): "Adult" means an individual who has attained 18 years of age.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(2): Title 75, Chapter 5, Part 4, Protection of Property of Persons Under Disability and Minors "Conservator" means a person appointed by the court to administer the property of an adult, including a person appointed under
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(3): "Emergency" means circumstances that likely will result in substantial harm to a respondent's health, safety, or welfare, and in which the appointment of a guardian is necessary because no other person has authority to and is willing to act on the respondent's behalf.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(4): Title 75, Chapter 5, Part 3, Guardians of Incapacitated Persons "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make decisions regarding the person of an adult, including a person appointed under
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(5): "Guardianship order" means an order appointing a guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(6): "Guardianship proceeding" means a proceeding in which an order for the appointment of a guardian is sought or has been issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(7): "Home state" means the state in which the respondent was physically present for at least six consecutive months immediately before the filing of a petition for the appointment of a guardian or protective order.  A period of temporary absence counts as part of the six-month period.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(8): "Incapacitated person" means an adult for whom a guardian has been appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(9): "Party" means the respondent, petitioner, guardian, conservator, or any other person allowed by the court to participate in a guardianship or protective proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(10): "Person," except in the terms "incapacitated person" or "protected person," means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust, partnership, limited liability company, association, joint venture, government or governmental subdivision, agency or instrumentality, public corporation, or any other legal or commercial entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(11): "Protected person" means an adult for whom a protective order has been made.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(12): "Protective order" means an order appointing a conservator or another court order related to management of an adult's property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(13): "Protective proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which a protective order is sought or has been issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(14): "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in perceivable form.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(15): "Respondent" means an adult for whom a protective order or the appointment of a guardian is sought.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(16): "Significant-connection state" means a state, other than the home state, with which a respondent has a significant connection other than mere physical presence and in which substantial evidence concerning the respondent is available.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-102(17): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, a federally recognized Indian tribe, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.

----------------------------------------------------------
A court of this state may treat a foreign country as if it were a state for the purpose of applying

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-104(2): Courts may communicate concerning schedules, calendars, court records, and other administrative matters without making a record.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(1)(a): hold an evidentiary hearing;

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(1)(c): order that an evaluation or assessment be made of the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(1)(d): order any appropriate investigation of a person involved in a proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(1)(e): (1)(a); (1)(b); (1)(c); (d) forward to the court of this state a certified copy of the transcript or other record of a hearing under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(1)(f): issue any order necessary to assure the appearance in the proceeding of a person whose presence is necessary for the court to make a determination, including the respondent or the incapacitated or protected person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(1)(g): issue an order authorizing the release of medical, financial, criminal, or other relevant information in that state, including protected health information as defined in 45 Code of Federal Regulations Section 164.504.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-105(2): (1) If a court of another state in which a guardianship or protective proceeding is pending requests assistance of the kind provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-106 Taking testimony in another state.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-106(1): In a guardianship or protective proceeding, in addition to other procedures that may be available, testimony of a witness who is located in another state may be offered by deposition or other means allowable in this state for testimony taken in another state.  The court on its own motion may order that the testimony of a witness be taken in another state and may prescribe the manner in which and the terms upon which the testimony is to be taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-106(2): In a guardianship or protective proceeding, a court in this state may permit a witness located in another state to be deposed or to testify by telephone, audiovisual, or other electronic means.  A court of this state shall cooperate with courts of other states in designating an appropriate location for the deposition or testimony.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-106(3): Documentary evidence transmitted from another state to a court of this state by technological means that do not produce an original writing may not be excluded from evidence on an objection based on the best evidence rule.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201 Exclusive basis -- Significant connection.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201(1): This part provides the exclusive jurisdictional basis for a court of this state to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order for an adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201(2): 75-5b-203; 75-5b-301(5) In determining under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201(2)(a): the location of the respondent's family and other persons required to be notified of the guardianship or protective proceeding;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201(2)(b): the length of time the respondent at any time was physically present in the state and the duration of any absence;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201(2)(c): the location of the respondent's property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-201(2)(d): the extent to which the respondent has ties to the state such as voting registration, state or local tax return filing, vehicle registration, driver license, social relationship, and receipt of services.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202 Jurisdiction.
---------------------------------------------
A court of this state has jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order for a respondent if:Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(1): this state is the respondent's home state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(2): 75-5b-205 on the date the petition is filed, this state is a significant-connection state and:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(2)(a): the respondent does not have a home state or a court of the respondent's home state has declined to exercise jurisdiction because this state is a more appropriate forum; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(2)(b): 75-5b-205 the respondent has a home state, a petition for an appointment or order is not pending in a court of that state or another significant-connection state, and, before the court makes the appointment or issues the order:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(2)(b)(i): a petition for an appointment or order is not filed in the respondent's home state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(2)(b)(ii): an objection to the court's jurisdiction is not filed by a person required to be notified of the proceeding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(2)(b)(iii): 75-5b-205 the court in this state concludes that it is an appropriate forum under the factors set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(3): (1); (2) this state does not have jurisdiction under either Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-202(4): 75-5b-204 the requirements for special jurisdiction under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-203 Special jurisdiction.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-203(1): 75-5b-202; 75-5b-301 A court of this state lacking jurisdiction under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-203(1)(a): appoint a guardian in an emergency for a term not exceeding 90 days for a respondent who is physically present in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-203(1)(b): issue a protective order with respect to real or tangible personal property located in this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-203(1)(c): 75-5b-301 appoint a guardian or conservator for an incapacitated or protected person for whom a provisional order to transfer the proceeding from another state has been issued under procedures similar to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-203(2): If a petition for the appointment of a guardian in an emergency is brought in this state and this state was not the respondent's home state on the date the petition was filed, the court shall dismiss the proceeding at the request of the court of the home state, if any, whether dismissal is requested before or after the emergency appointment.

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205 Declining jurisdiction if another court is a more appropriate forum.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(1): 75-5b-202 A court of this state having jurisdiction under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(2): (1) If a court of this state declines to exercise its jurisdiction under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3): In determining whether it is an appropriate forum, the court shall consider all relevant factors, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(a): any expressed preference of the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(b): whether abuse, neglect, or exploitation of the respondent has occurred or is likely to occur and which state could best protect the respondent from the abuse, neglect, or exploitation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(c): the length of time the respondent was physically located in or was a legal resident of this or another state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(d): the distance of the respondent from the court in each state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(e): the financial circumstances of the respondent's estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(f): the nature and location of the evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(g): the ability of the court in each state to decide the issue expeditiously and the procedures necessary to present evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(h): the familiarity of the court of each state with the facts and issues in the proceeding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-205(3)(i): if an appointment were made, the court's ability to monitor the conduct of the guardian or conservator.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206 Jurisdiction declined by reason of conduct.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1): 75-5b-205(3); 75-5b-202 If at any time a court of this state determines that it acquired jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order because of unjustifiable conduct, the court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1)(a): decline to exercise jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1)(b): exercise jurisdiction for the limited purpose of fashioning an appropriate remedy to ensure the health, safety, and welfare of the respondent or the protection of the respondent's property or prevent a repetition of the unjustifiable conduct, including staying the proceeding until a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective order is filed in a court of another state having jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1)(c): 75-5b-205(3); 75-5b-202 continue to exercise jurisdiction after considering:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1)(c)(i): the extent to which the respondent and all persons required to be notified of the proceedings have acquiesced in the exercise of the court's jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1)(c)(ii): 75-5b-205(3) whether it is a more appropriate forum than the court of any other state under the factors set forth in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(1)(c)(iii): 75-5b-202 whether the court of any other state would have jurisdiction under factual circumstances in substantial conformity with the jurisdictional standards of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-206(2): If a court of this state determines that it acquired jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order because a party seeking to invoke its jurisdiction engaged in unjustifiable conduct, it may assess against that party necessary and reasonable expenses, including attorney fees, investigative fees, court costs, communication expenses, witness fees and expenses, and travel expenses.  The court may not assess fees, costs, or expenses of any kind against the state or a governmental subdivision, agency, or instrumentality of the state unless authorized by law other than this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-207 Notice of proceeding.
-----------------------------------------------------
If a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective order is brought in this state and this state was not the respondent's home state on the date the petition was filed, in addition to complying with the notice requirements of this state, notice of the petition shall be given to those persons who would be entitled to notice of the petition if the proceeding were brought in the respondent's home state.  The notice shall be given in the same manner as notice is given in this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301 Transfer of guardianship or conservatorship to another state.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(1): A guardian or conservator appointed in this state may petition the court to transfer the guardianship or conservatorship to another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(2): (1) Notice of a petition under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(3): (1) On the court's own motion or on request of the guardian or conservator, the incapacitated or protected person, or other person required to be notified of the petition, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition filed pursuant to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(4): The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition to transfer a guardianship and shall direct the guardian to petition for guardianship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the guardianship will be accepted by the court in the other state and the court finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(4)(a): the incapacitated person is physically present in or is reasonably expected to move permanently to the other state;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(4)(b): an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be contrary to the interests of the incapacitated person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(4)(c): plans for care and services for the incapacitated person in the other state are reasonable and sufficient.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(5): 75-5b-201(2) The court shall issue a provisional order granting a petition to transfer a conservatorship and shall direct the conservator to petition for conservatorship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the conservatorship will be accepted by the court of the other state and the court finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(5)(a): 75-5b-201(2) the protected person is physically present in or is reasonably expected to move permanently to the other state, or the protected person has a significant connection to the other state considering the factors in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(5)(b): an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be contrary to the interests of the protected person; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(5)(c): adequate arrangements will be made for management of the protected person's property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(6): 75-5b-302 The court shall issue a final order confirming the transfer and terminating the guardianship or conservatorship upon its receipt of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(6)(a): 75-5b-302 a provisional order accepting the proceeding from the court to which the proceeding is to be transferred which is issued under provisions similar to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-301(6)(b): the documents required to terminate a guardianship or conservatorship in this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-5b-302(7): In granting a petition under this section, the court shall recognize a guardianship or conservatorship order from the other state, including the determination of the incapacitated or protected person's incapacity and the appointment of the guardian or conservator.
