Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-105(2)(j): 75-7-203; 75-7-205 the jurisdiction and venue requirements for an action involving a trust as described in Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-106 Common law of trusts -- Principles of equity.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The common law of trusts and principles of equity supplement this chapter, except to the extent modified by this chapter or laws of this state.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107 Governing law.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(1)(a): "Foreign trust" means a trust that is created in another state or country and valid in the state or country in which the trust is created.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(1)(b): "State law provision" means a provision that the laws of a named state govern the validity, construction, and administration of a trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(2): If a trust has a state law provision specifying this state, the validity, construction, and administration of the trust are to be governed by the laws of this state if any administration of the trust is done in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(3): For all trusts created on or after December 31, 2003, if a trust does not have a state law provision, the validity, construction, and administration of the trust are to be governed by the laws of this state if the trust is administered in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(4): A trust shall be considered to be administered in this state if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(4)(a): the trust states that this state is the place of administration, and any administration of the trust is done in this state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(4)(b): the place of business where the fiduciary transacts a major portion of its administration of the trust is in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(5): 75B-1-302 If a foreign trust is administered in this state as provided in this section, the following provisions are effective and enforceable under the laws of this state:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(5)(a): 75B-1-302 a provision in the trust that restricts the transfer of trust assets in a manner similar to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(5)(b): a provision that allows the trust to be perpetual; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(5)(c): a provision that is not expressly prohibited by the law of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(6): A foreign trust that moves its administration to this state is valid whether or not the trust complied with the laws of this state at the time of the trust's creation or after the trust's creation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-107(7): Unless otherwise designated in the trust instrument, a trust is administered in this state if it meets the requirements of Subsection (4).


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108 Principal place of administration.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(1): Without precluding other means for establishing a sufficient connection with the designated jurisdiction, terms of a trust designating the principal place of administration are valid and controlling if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(1)(a): a trustee's principal place of business is located in or a trustee is a resident of the designated jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(1)(b): all or part of the administration occurs in the designated jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(2): A trustee is under a continuing duty to administer the trust at a place appropriate to its purposes, its administration, and the interests of the beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(3): (2) Without precluding the right of the court to order, approve, or disapprove a transfer, the trustee, in furtherance of the duty prescribed by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(4): The trustee shall notify the qualified beneficiaries of a proposed transfer of a trust's principal place of administration not less than 60 days before initiating the transfer.  The notice of proposed transfer must include:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(4)(a): the name of the jurisdiction to which the principal place of administration is to be transferred;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(4)(b): the address and telephone number at the new location at which the trustee can be contacted;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(4)(c): an explanation of the reasons for the proposed transfer;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(4)(d): the date on which the proposed transfer is anticipated to occur; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(4)(e): the date, not less than 60 days after the giving of the notice, by which the qualified beneficiary must notify the trustee of an objection to the proposed transfer.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(5): The authority of a trustee under this section to transfer a trust's principal place of administration terminates if a qualified beneficiary notifies the trustee of an objection to the proposed transfer on or before the date specified in the notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-108(6): 75-7-704 In connection with a transfer of the trust's principal place of administration, the trustee may transfer some or all of the trust property to a successor trustee designated in the terms of the trust or appointed pursuant to Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-109 Methods and waiver of notice.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-109(1): Notice to a person under this chapter or the sending of a document to a person under this chapter must be accomplished in a manner reasonably suitable under the circumstances and likely to result in receipt of the notice or document.  Permissible methods of notice or for sending a document include first-class mail, personal delivery, delivery to the person's last known place of residence or place of business, or a properly directed electronic message.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-109(2): Notice under this chapter or the sending of a document under this chapter may be waived by the person to be notified or sent the document.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-109(3): Notice of a judicial proceeding must be given as provided in the applicable rules of civil procedure.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110 Nonjudicial settlement agreements.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(1): For purposes of this section, "interested persons" means persons whose consent would be required in order to achieve a binding settlement were the settlement to be approved by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(2): (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(3): A nonjudicial settlement agreement is valid only to the extent it does not violate a material purpose of the trust and includes terms and conditions that could be properly approved by the court under this chapter or other applicable law.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4): Matters that may be resolved by a nonjudicial settlement agreement include:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4)(a): the interpretation or construction of the terms of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4)(b): the approval of a trustee's report or accounting;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4)(c): direction to a trustee to refrain from performing a particular act or the grant to a trustee of any necessary or desirable power;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4)(d): the resignation or appointment of a trustee and the determination of a trustee's compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4)(e): transfer of a trust's principal place of administration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(4)(f): liability of a trustee for an action relating to the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-110(5): Part 3, Representation Any interested person may request the court to approve a nonjudicial settlement agreement, to determine whether the representation as provided in


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-111 Rules of construction.
-----------------------------------------------------
The rules of construction that apply to the interpretation of and disposition of property by will or other governing instrument, as defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-112 Penalty provisions.
--------------------------------------------------
A provision in a trust instrument purporting to penalize a beneficiary by charging the beneficiary's interest in the trust, or to penalize the beneficiary in another manner, for instituting a proceeding to challenge the acts of the trustee or other fiduciary of a trust, or for instituting other proceedings relating to the trust is unenforceable if probable cause exists for instituting the proceedings.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201 Court -- Exclusive jurisdiction of trusts.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(a): The court has exclusive jurisdiction of proceedings initiated by interested parties concerning the internal affairs of trusts.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(b): Proceedings which may be maintained under this section are those concerning:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(b)(i): the administration and distribution of trusts;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(b)(ii): the declaration of rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(b)(iii): the determination of other matters involving trustees and beneficiaries of trusts.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c): These include, but are not limited to proceedings to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(i): appoint or remove a trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(ii): review a trustee's fees;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(iii): review and settle interim or final accounts;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(iv): ascertain beneficiaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(v): determine any question arising in the administration or distribution of any trust, including questions of construction of trust instruments;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(vi): instruct trustees;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(vii): determine the existence or nonexistence of any immunity, power, privilege, duty, or right; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(1)(c)(viii): order transfer of administration of the trust to another state upon appropriate conditions as may be determined by the court or accept transfer of administration of a trust from another state to this state upon such conditions as may be imposed by the supervising court of the other state, unless the court in this state determines that these conditions are incompatible with its own rules and procedures.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(2)(a): A proceeding under this section does not result in continuing supervision by the court over the administration of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-201(2)(b): The management and distribution of a trust estate, submission of accounts and reports to beneficiaries, payment of trustee's fees and other obligations of a trust, acceptance and change of trusteeship, and other aspects of the administration of a trust shall proceed expeditiously consistent with the terms of the trust, free of judicial intervention and without order, approval or other action of any court, subject to the jurisdiction of the court as invoked by interested parties or as otherwise exercised as provided by law.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-202 Effect of administration in this state -- Consent to jurisdiction.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-202(1): The trustee submits personally to the jurisdiction of the courts of this state regarding any matter involving the trust if  the trustee acts as trustee of a trust administered in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-202(2): To the extent of the beneficial interests in a trust administered in this state, the beneficiaries of the trust are subject to the jurisdiction of the courts of this state regarding any matter involving the trust.  By accepting a distribution from such a trust, the recipient submits personally to the jurisdiction of the courts of this state regarding any matter involving the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-202(3): By accepting the delegation of a trust function from the trustee of a trust administered in this state, the agent submits to the jurisdiction of the courts of this state regarding any matter involving the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-202(4): 75-7-107(4) Unless otherwise designated in the trust instrument, a trust is administered in this state if it meets the requirements of Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-203 Jurisdiction over an action involving a trust.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-203(1): A court of this state has jurisdiction as described in Title 78A, Judiciary and Judicial Administration, over an action involving a trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-203(2): This section does not preclude judicial or nonjudicial alternative dispute resolution.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204 Trust proceedings -- Dismissal of matters relating to foreign trusts.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(1): 75-7-201 The court may not, over the objection of a party, entertain proceedings under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(1)(a): is under the continuing supervision of a foreign court;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(1)(b): is registered in another state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(1)(c): has a fiduciary which transacts a major portion of its trust administration in another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(2): (1) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(2)(a): all appropriate parties could not be bound by litigation in the courts of the other state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(2)(b): the interests of justice would be seriously impaired.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-204(3): The court may condition a stay or dismissal of a proceeding on the consent of any party to the jurisdiction of the courts of another state, or the court may grant a continuance or enter any other appropriate order.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205 Venue.
-------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(1): Notwithstanding Title 78B, Chapter 3a, Venue for Civil Actions, and except as provided in Subsection (2), a person shall bring an action involving a trust, if the action is brought in the district court, in:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(1)(a): the county in which the trust's principal place of administration is or will be located; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(1)(b): if the trust is created by a will and the estate is not yet closed, the county in which the decedent's estate is being administered.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(2): Notwithstanding Title 78B, Chapter 3a, Venue for Civil Actions, and if a trust has no trustee, a person shall bring an action for the appointment of a trustee, if the action is brought in the district court, in:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(2)(a): a county of this state in which a beneficiary resides;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(2)(b): a county in which any trust property is located; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-205(2)(c): if the trust is created by a will, the county in which the decedent's estate was or is being administered.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-301 Basic effect.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-301(1): Notice to a person who may represent and bind another person under this part has the same effect as if notice were given directly to the other person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-301(2): The consent of a person who may represent and bind another person under this part is binding on the person represented unless the person represented objects to the representation before the consent would otherwise have become effective.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-301(3): 75-7-411; 75B-1-302 Except as otherwise provided in Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-302 Representation by holder of general testamentary power of appointment.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent there is no conflict of interest between the holder of a general testamentary power of appointment and the persons represented with respect to the particular question or dispute, the holder may represent and bind persons whose interests, as permissible appointees, takers in default, or otherwise, are subject to the power.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303 Representation by fiduciaries and parents.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent there is no conflict of interest between the representative and the person represented or among those being represented with respect to a particular question or dispute:Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303(1): a conservator may represent and bind the protected person whose estate the conservator controls;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303(2): a guardian may represent and bind the ward if a conservator of the ward's estate has not been appointed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303(3): an agent having authority to act with respect to the particular question or dispute may represent and bind the principal;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303(4): a trustee may represent and bind the beneficiaries of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303(5): a personal representative of a decedent's estate may represent and bind persons interested in the estate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-303(6): a parent may represent and bind the parent's minor or unborn child if a conservator or guardian for the child has not been appointed.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-304 Representation by person having substantially identical interest.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless otherwise represented, a minor, incapacitated, or unborn individual, or a person whose identity or location is unknown and not reasonably ascertainable, may be represented by and bound by another having a substantially identical interest with respect to the particular question or dispute, but only to the extent there is no conflict of interest between the representative and the person represented.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-305 Appointment of guardian ad litem or other representative.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-305(1): If the court determines that an interest is not represented under this part, or that the otherwise available representation might be inadequate, the court may appoint a guardian ad litem or other representative to receive notice, give consent, and otherwise represent, bind, and act on behalf of a minor, incapacitated or protected person, or unborn individual, or a person whose identity or location is unknown.  A guardian ad litem or other representative may be appointed to represent several persons or interests.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-305(2): A guardian ad litem or other representative may act on behalf of the individual represented with respect to any matter arising under this chapter, whether or not a judicial proceeding concerning the trust is pending.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-305(3): In making decisions, a guardian ad litem or other representative may consider general benefit accruing to the living members of the individual's family.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-401 Methods of creating trust.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-401(1): A trust may be created by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-401(1)(a): transfer of property to another person as trustee during the settlor's lifetime or by will or other disposition taking effect upon the settlor's death;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-401(1)(b): declaration by the owner of property that the owner holds identifiable property as trustee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-401(1)(c): exercise of a power of appointment in favor of a trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-401(2): A health savings account is established on the first day an individual is covered by a high deductible health plan, as defined in Section 223 of the Internal Revenue Code.  The health savings account shall be opened with a trustee or custodian within the time prescribed by law, without extensions, for filing a federal income tax return for that year.  A health savings account is established regardless of a transfer of cash or other property to the account and, unless required by the trustee or custodian, it is not necessary for any party to sign a health savings account trust or custodial agreement regarding the health savings account.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402 Requirements for creation.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1): 75-2-1001; 75-2-1001 A trust is created only if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(a): the settlor has capacity to create a trust, which standard of capacity shall be the same as for a person to create a will;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(b): the settlor indicates an intention to create the trust or a statute, judgment, or decree authorizes the creation of a trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(c): 75-2-1001; 75-2-1001 the trust has a definite beneficiary or is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(c)(i): a charitable trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(c)(ii): 75-2-1001 a trust for the care of an animal, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(c)(iii): 75-2-1001 a trust for a noncharitable purpose, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(d): the trustee has duties to perform; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(1)(e): the same person is not the sole trustee and sole beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(2): A beneficiary is definite if the beneficiary can be ascertained now or in the future, subject to any applicable rule against perpetuities.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-402(3): A power in a trustee to select a beneficiary from an indefinite class is valid.  If the power is not exercised within a reasonable time, the power fails and the property subject to the power passes to the persons who would have taken the property had the power not been conferred.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-403 Trusts created in other jurisdictions.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
A trust not created by will is validly created if its creation complies with the law of the jurisdiction in which the trust instrument was executed, or the law of the jurisdiction in which, at the time of creation:Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-403(1): the settlor was domiciled, had a place of abode, or was a national;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-403(2): a trustee was domiciled or had a place of business; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-403(3): any trust property was located.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-404 Trust purposes.
----------------------------------------------
A trust may be created only to the extent its purposes are lawful, not contrary to public policy, and possible to achieve.  A trust and its terms must be for the benefit of its beneficiaries.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-405 Charitable purposes -- Enforcement.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-405(1): A charitable trust may be created for the relief of poverty, the advancement of education or religion, the promotion of health, governmental or municipal purposes, or other purposes the achievement of which is beneficial to the community.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-405(2): If the terms of a charitable trust do not indicate a particular charitable purpose or beneficiary, the trustee, if authorized by the terms of the trust, or if not, the court may select one or more charitable purposes or beneficiaries.  The selection must be consistent with the settlor's intention to the extent it can be ascertained.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-405(3): The settlor of a charitable trust, among others, may maintain a proceeding to enforce the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-406 Creation of trust induced by fraud, duress, or undue influence.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A trust is void to the extent its creation was induced by fraud, duress, or undue influence.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-407 Evidence of oral trust.
------------------------------------------------------
Except as required by a statute other than this chapter, a trust need not be evidenced by a trust instrument, but the creation of an oral trust and its terms may be established only by clear and convincing evidence.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-408 Trust for care of animal.
--------------------------------------------------------
A trust may be created to provide for the care of a pet or animal as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-409 Noncharitable trust without ascertainable beneficiary.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A trust may be created for a noncharitable purpose without a definite or definitely ascertainable beneficiary or for a noncharitable but otherwise valid purpose to be selected by the trustee as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-410 Modification or termination of trust -- Proceedings for approval or disapproval.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-410(1): 75-7-411; 75-7-414 In addition to the methods of termination prescribed by Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-410(2): 75-7-411; 75-7-416; 75-7-417; 75-7-411; 75-7-413 A proceeding to approve or disapprove a proposed modification or termination under Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411 Modification or termination of noncharitable irrevocable trust by consent.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(1): A noncharitable, irrevocable trust may be modified or terminated upon consent of the settlor and all beneficiaries, even if the modification or termination is inconsistent with a material purpose of the trust.  A settlor's power to consent to a trust's termination may be exercised by an agent under a power of attorney only to the extent expressly authorized by the power of attorney or the terms of the trust, by the settlor's conservator with the approval of the court supervising the conservatorship if an agent is not so authorized, or by the settlor's guardian with the approval of the court supervising the guardianship if an agent is not so authorized and a conservator has not been appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(2): A noncharitable, irrevocable trust may be terminated upon consent of all of the beneficiaries if the court concludes that continuance of the trust is not necessary to achieve any material purpose of the trust.  A noncharitable, irrevocable trust may be modified upon consent of all of the beneficiaries if the court concludes that modification is not inconsistent with a material purpose of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(3): A spendthrift provision in the terms of the trust is not presumed to constitute a material purpose of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(4): (1); (2) Upon termination of a trust under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(5): (1); (2) If not all of the beneficiaries consent to a proposed modification or termination of the trust under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(5)(a): if all of the beneficiaries had consented, the trust could have been modified or terminated under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-411(5)(b): the interests of a beneficiary who does not consent will be adequately protected.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-412 Modification or termination because of unanticipated circumstances or inability to administer trust effectively.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-412(1): The court may modify the administrative or dispositive terms of a trust or terminate the trust if, because of circumstances not anticipated by the settlor, modification or termination will further the purposes of the trust.  To the extent practicable, the modification must be made in accordance with the settlor's probable intention.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-412(2): The court may modify the administrative terms of a trust if continuation of the trust on its existing terms would be impracticable or wasteful or impair the trust's administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-412(3): Upon termination of a trust under this section, the trustee shall distribute the trust property as directed by the court or otherwise in a manner consistent with the purposes of the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413 Cy pres.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(1): (2) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(1)(a): the trust does not fail, in whole or in part;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(1)(b): the trust property does not revert to the settlor or the settlor's successors in interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(1)(c): the court may apply cy pres to modify or terminate the trust by directing that the trust property be applied or distributed, in whole or in part, in a manner consistent with the settlor's charitable purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(2): (1) A provision in the terms of a charitable trust that would result in distribution of the trust property to a noncharitable beneficiary prevails over the power of the court under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(2)(a): the trust property is to revert to the settlor and the settlor is still living; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-413(2)(b): fewer than 21 years have elapsed since the date of the trust's creation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-414 Modification or termination of uneconomic trust.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-414(1): After notice to the qualified beneficiaries, the trustee of a trust consisting of trust property having a total value less than $100,000 may terminate the trust if the trustee concludes that the value of the trust property is insufficient to justify the cost of administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-414(2): The court may modify or terminate a trust or remove the trustee and appoint a different trustee if it determines that the value of the trust property is insufficient to justify the cost of administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-414(3): Upon termination of a trust under this section, the trustee shall distribute the trust property in a manner consistent with the purposes of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-414(4): This section does not apply to an easement for conservation or preservation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-415 Reformation to correct mistakes.
---------------------------------------------------------------
The court may reform the terms of a trust, even if unambiguous, to conform the terms to the settlor's intention if it is proved by clear and convincing evidence that both the settlor's intent and the terms of the trust were affected by a mistake of fact or law, whether in expression or inducement.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-416 Modification to achieve settlor's tax objectives.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
To achieve the settlor's tax objectives, the court may modify the terms of a trust in order to achieve the settlor's tax objectives.  The court may provide that the modification has retroactive effect.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-417 Combination and division of trusts.
------------------------------------------------------------------
After notice to the qualified beneficiaries, a trustee may combine two or more trusts into a single trust or divide a trust into two or more separate trusts, if the result does not impair rights of any beneficiary or adversely affect achievement of the purposes of the trust.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-501 Rights of beneficiary's creditor or assignee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
To the extent a beneficiary's interest is not protected by a spendthrift provision or Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-502 Spendthrift provisions for beneficiaries other than the settlor.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-502(1): A spendthrift provision for a beneficiary other than the settlor is valid only if it restrains both voluntary and involuntary transfer of a beneficiary's interest, even if the beneficiary is the trustee or cotrustee of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-502(2): A term of a trust providing that the interest of a beneficiary other than the settlor is held subject to a "spendthrift trust," or words of similar import, is sufficient to restrain both voluntary and involuntary transfer of the beneficiary's interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-502(3): A beneficiary may not transfer an interest in a trust in violation of a valid spendthrift provision and, except as otherwise provided in this part, a creditor or assignee of the beneficiary may not reach the interest or a distribution by the trustee before its receipt by the beneficiary.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503 Exceptions to spendthrift provision.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(1): 77-32b-102; 77-32b-102; 77-38b-102; 77-38b-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(1)(a): "Child" includes any person for whom an order or judgment for child support has been entered in this or another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(1)(b): 77-32b-102 "Civil accounts receivable" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(1)(c): 77-32b-102 "Civil restitution of judgment" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(1)(d): 77-38b-102 "Restitution" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(1)(e): 77-38b-102 "Victim" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(2): Title 77, Chapter 38b, Crime Victims Restitution Act; 63A-3-502 Even if a trust contains a spendthrift provision, the following persons may obtain an order from a court that attaches present or future distributions to the beneficiary:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(2)(a): a beneficiary's child who has a judgment or court order against the beneficiary for support or maintenance;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(2)(b): a judgment creditor who has provided services for the protection of a beneficiary's interest in the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(2)(c): Title 77, Chapter 38b, Crime Victims Restitution Act a victim who has a judgment requiring the beneficiary to pay restitution in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(2)(d): 63A-3-502 the Office of State Debt Collection, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-503(3): A spendthrift provision is unenforceable against a claim of this state or the United States to the extent a statute of this state or federal law so provides.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504 Discretionary trusts -- Effect of standard.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(1): In this section, "child" includes any person for whom an order or judgment for child support has been entered in this or another state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(2): (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(2)(a): the discretion is expressed in the form of a standard of distribution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(2)(b): the trustee has abused the discretion.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(3): To the extent a trustee has not complied with a standard of distribution or has abused a discretion:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(3)(a): a distribution may be ordered by the court to satisfy a judgment or court order against the beneficiary for support or maintenance of the beneficiary's child, spouse, or former spouse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(3)(b): the court shall direct the trustee to pay to the child, spouse, or former spouse such amount as is equitable under the circumstances but not more than the amount the trustee would have been required to distribute to or for the benefit of the beneficiary had the trustee complied with the standard or not abused the discretion.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-504(4): This section does not limit the right of a beneficiary to maintain a judicial proceeding against a trustee for an abuse of discretion or failure to comply with a standard for distribution.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505 Creditor's claim against settlor.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Regardless of whether the terms of a trust contain a spendthrift provision, the following rules apply:Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(1): During the lifetime of the settlor, the property of a revocable trust is subject to the claims of the settlor's creditors.  If a revocable trust has more than one settlor, the amount the creditor or assignee of a particular settlor may reach may not exceed the settlor's interest in the portion of the trust attributable to that settlor's contribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2): 75B-1-302; 75B-1-302
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2)(a): 75B-1-302 With respect to an irrevocable trust other than an irrevocable trust that meets the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2)(b): 75B-1-302 With respect to an irrevocable trust that has more than one settlor, other than an irrevocable trust that meets the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2)(c): Notwithstanding Subsections (2)(a) and (b), a creditor of a settlor may not satisfy the creditor's claim from an irrevocable trust solely because the trustee may make a discretionary distribution reimbursing the settlor for income tax liability of the settlor attributable to the income of the irrevocable trust, when the distribution is:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2)(c)(i): subject to the discretion of a trustee who is not the settlor;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2)(c)(ii): subject to the consent of an advisor who is not the settlor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(2)(c)(iii): at the direction of an advisor who is not the settlor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-505(3): After the death of a settlor, and subject to the settlor's right to direct the source from which liabilities will be paid, the property of a trust that was revocable at the settlor's death, but not property received by the trust as a result of the death of the settlor which is otherwise exempt from the claims of the settlor's creditors, is subject to claims of the settlor's creditors, costs of administration of the settlor's estate, the expenses of the settlor's funeral and disposal of remains, and statutory allowances to a surviving spouse and children to the extent the settlor's probate estate is inadequate to satisfy those claims, costs, expenses, and allowances.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-506 Overdue distribution.
----------------------------------------------------
Whether or not a trust contains a spendthrift provision, a creditor or assignee of a beneficiary may reach a mandatory distribution of income or principal, including a distribution upon termination of the trust, if the trustee has not made the distribution to the beneficiary within a reasonable time after the required distribution date.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-507 Personal obligations of trustee.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Trust property is not subject to personal obligations of the trustee, even if the trustee becomes insolvent or bankrupt.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-508 Notice to creditors.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-510 Manner of presentation of claims.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-510(1): Claims against a deceased settlor's estate or inter vivos revocable trust shall be presented as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-510(1)(a): The claimant may deliver or mail to the trustee, or the trustee's attorney of record, a written statement of the claim indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant, and the amount claimed.  The claim is considered presented upon the receipt of the written statement of claim by the trustee or the trustee's attorney of record.  If a claim is not yet due, the date when it will become due shall be stated.  If the claim is contingent or unliquidated, the nature of the uncertainty shall be stated.  If the claim is secured, the security shall be described.  Failure to describe correctly the security, the nature of any uncertainty, and the due date of a claim not yet due does not invalidate the presentation made.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-510(1)(b): The claimant may commence a proceeding against the trustee in any court where the trustee may be subjected to jurisdiction to obtain payment of the claim against the deceased settlor's estate or the trust estate, but the commencement of the proceeding must occur within the time limited for presenting the claim.  No presentation of claim is required in regard to matters claimed in proceedings against the deceased settlor which were pending at the time of the deceased settlor's death.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-510(2): (1)(a) If a claim is presented under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511 Classification of claims.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1): 26B-3-1013 If the applicable assets of the deceased settlor's estate or trust estate are insufficient to pay all claims in full, the trustee shall make payment in the following order:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1)(a): reasonable funeral expenses;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1)(b): costs and expenses of administration;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1)(c): debts and taxes with preference under federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1)(d): 26B-3-1013 reasonable and necessary medical and hospital expenses of the last illness of the deceased settlor, including compensation of persons attending the deceased settlor, and medical assistance if Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1)(e): debts and taxes with preference under other laws of this state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(1)(f): all other claims.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-511(2): No preference shall be given in the payment of any claim over any other claim of the same class, and a claim due and payable shall not be entitled to a preference over claims not due.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-512 Allowance of claims.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-512(1): 75-7-510; 75-7-509 As to claims presented in the manner described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-512(2): (1) Upon the petition of the trustee or a claimant in a proceeding for this purpose, the court may order any claim presented to the trustee or trustee's attorney in a timely manner and not barred by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-512(3): A judgment in a proceeding in another court against the trustee to enforce a claim against a deceased settlor's estate is a court-ordered allowance of the claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-512(4): Unless otherwise provided in any judgment in another court entered against a trustee, allowed claims bear interest at the legal rate for the period commencing six months after the deceased settlor's date of death unless based on a contract making a provision for interest, in which case they bear interest in accordance with that provision.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-513 Payment of claims.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-513(1): 75-7-509 Upon the expiration of the earliest of the time limitations provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-513(2): (1) The trustee at any time may pay any just claim that has not been barred, with or without formal presentation, but the trustee shall be personally liable to any other claimant whose claim is allowed and who is injured by the payment if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-513(2)(a): (1) the payment was made before the expiration of the time limit stated in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-513(2)(b): the payment was made, due to the negligence or willful fault of the trustee, in a way that deprived the injured claimant of his priority.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-514 Secured claims.
----------------------------------------------
Payment of a secured claim shall be upon the basis of the amount allowed if the creditor surrenders his security; but otherwise payment shall be based upon one of the following:Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-514(1): if the creditor exhausts his security before receiving payment, unless precluded by another provision of the law, upon the amount of the claim allowed less the fair value of the security; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-514(2): if the creditor does not have the right to exhaust his security or has not done so, upon the amount of the claim allowed less the value of the security determined by converting it into money according to the terms of the agreement pursuant to which the security was delivered to the creditor, or by the creditor and trustee by agreement, arbitration, compromise, or litigation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-515 Claims not due and contingent or unliquidated claims.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-515(1): If a claim which will become due at a future time or a contingent or unliquidated claim becomes due or certain before the distribution of the trust estate, and if the claim has been allowed or established by a proceeding, it shall be paid in the same manner as presently due and absolute claims of the same class.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-515(2): In other cases the trustee, or, on petition of the trustee or the claimant in a special proceeding for that purpose, the court, may provide for payment as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-515(2)(a): if the claimant consents, he may be paid the present or agreed value of the claim, taking any uncertainty into account; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-515(2)(b): arrangement for future payment, or possible payment, on the happening of the contingency or on liquidation may be made by creating a trust, giving a mortgage, obtaining a bond or security from a beneficiary, or otherwise.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-516 Counterclaims.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-516(1): In allowing a claim, the trustee may deduct any counterclaim which the deceased settlor's estate has against the claimant.  In determining a claim against a deceased settlor's estate, a court shall reduce the amount allowed by the amount of any counterclaims and, if the counterclaims exceed the claim, render a judgment against the claimant in the amount of the excess.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-516(2): A counterclaim, liquidated or unliquidated, may arise from a transaction other than that upon which the claim is based.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-516(3): A counterclaim may give rise to relief exceeding in amount or different in kind from that sought in the claim.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-517 Execution and levies prohibited.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-517(1): No execution may issue upon nor may any levy be made against any property of the deceased settlor's estate under any judgment against a deceased settlor or a trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-517(2): This section may not be construed to prevent the enforcement of mortgages, pledges, or liens upon real or personal property in an appropriate proceeding.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-518 Compromise of claims.
----------------------------------------------------
When a claim against a deceased settlor's estate has been presented in any manner, the trustee may, if it appears in the best interest of the deceased settlor's estate, compromise the claim, whether due or not due, absolute or contingent, liquidated or unliquidated.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-519 Encumbered assets.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-519(1): If any assets of the deceased settlor's estate are encumbered by mortgage, pledge, lien, or other security interest, the trustee may pay the encumbrance or any part thereof, renew or extend any obligation secured by the encumbrance, or convey or transfer the assets to the creditor in satisfaction of his lien, in whole or in part, whether or not the holder of the encumbrance has presented a claim, if it appears to be in the best interest of the deceased settlor's estate.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-519(2): Payment of an encumbrance does not increase the share of the beneficiary entitled to the encumbered assets unless the beneficiary is entitled to exoneration or unless the terms of the deceased settlor's trust, under which the beneficiary is entitled to the encumbered assets, provides otherwise.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-604 Capacity of settlor of revocable trust.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
The capacity required to create, amend, revoke, or add property to a revocable trust, or to direct the actions of the trustee of a revocable trust, is the same as that required to make a will.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605 Revocation or amendment of revocable trust.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(1): (1) Unless the terms of a trust expressly provide that the trust is irrevocable, the settlor may revoke or amend the trust.  This Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(2): If a revocable trust is created or funded by more than one settlor:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(2)(a): to the extent the trust consists of community property, the trust may be revoked by either spouse acting alone but may be amended only by joint action of both spouses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(2)(b): to the extent the trust consists of property other than community property, each settlor may revoke or amend the trust with regard to the portion of the trust property attributable to that settlor's contribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(3): The settlor may revoke or amend a revocable trust:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(3)(a): by substantially complying with a method provided in the terms of the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(3)(b): if the terms of the trust do not provide a method or the method provided in the terms is not expressly made exclusive, by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(3)(b)(i): executing a later will or codicil that expressly refers to the trust or specifically devises property that would otherwise have passed according to the terms of the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(3)(b)(ii): any other method manifesting clear and convincing evidence of the settlor's intent.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(4): Upon revocation of a revocable trust, the trustee shall deliver the trust property as the settlor directs.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(5): A settlor's powers with respect to revocation, amendment, or distribution of trust property may be exercised by an agent under a power of attorney only to the extent expressly authorized by the terms of the trust or the power.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(6): A conservator of the settlor or, if no conservator has been appointed, a guardian of the settlor may exercise a settlor's powers with respect to revocation, amendment, or distribution of trust property only with the approval of the court supervising the conservatorship or guardianship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-605(7): A trustee who does not know that a trust has been revoked or amended is not liable to the settlor or settlor's successors in interest for distributions made and other actions taken on the assumption that the trust had not been amended or revoked.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606 Settlor's powers -- Powers of withdrawal.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606(1)(a): To the extent a trust is revocable by a settlor, a trustee may follow a direction of the settlor that is contrary to the terms of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606(1)(b): To the extent a trust is revocable by a settlor in conjunction with a person other than a trustee or a person holding an adverse interest, the trustee may follow a direction from the settlor and the other person holding the power to revoke even if the direction is contrary to the terms of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606(2): To the extent a trust is revocable and the settlor has capacity to revoke the trust, rights of the beneficiaries are subject to the control of, and the duties of the trustee are owed exclusively to, the settlor.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606(3): If a revocable trust has more than one settlor, the duties of the trustee are owed to all of the settlors having capacity to revoke the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-606(4): During the period the power may be exercised, the holder of a power of withdrawal has the rights of a settlor of a revocable trust under this section to the extent of the property subject to the power.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607 Limitation on action contesting validity of revocable trust -- Distribution of trust property.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(1): A person shall commence a judicial proceeding to contest the validity of a trust that was revocable at the settlor's death within the earlier of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(1)(a): three years after the settlor's death; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(1)(b): 90 days after the trustee sent the person a copy of the trust instrument and a notice informing the person of the trust's existence, of the trustee's name and address, and of the time allowed for commencing a proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(2): Upon the death of the settlor of a trust that was revocable at the settlor's death, the trustee may proceed to distribute the trust property in accordance with the terms of the trust.  The trustee is not subject to liability for doing so unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(2)(a): the trustee knows of a pending judicial proceeding contesting the validity of the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(2)(b): a potential contestant has notified the trustee of a possible judicial proceeding to contest the trust and a judicial proceeding is commenced within 60 days after the contestant sent the notification.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(3): With respect to a potential contest, the trustee is only liable for actions taken two or more business days after the trustee has actual receipt of written notice from a potential contestant.  The written notice shall include the name of the settlor or of the trust, the name of the potential contestant, and a description of the basis for the potential contest.  The written notice shall be mailed to the trustee at the principal place of administration of the trust by registered or certified mail, return receipt requested, or served upon the trustee in the same manner as a summons in a civil action.  Any other form or service of notice is not sufficient to impose liability on the trustee for actions taken pursuant to the terms of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-607(4): A beneficiary of a trust that is determined to have been invalid is liable to return any distribution received.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701 Accepting or declining trusteeship.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(1): (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(1)(a): by substantially complying with a method of acceptance provided in the terms of the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(1)(b): if the terms of the trust do not provide a method or the method provided in the terms is not expressly made exclusive, by accepting delivery of the trust property, exercising powers or performing duties as trustee, or otherwise indicating acceptance of the trusteeship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(2): A person designated as trustee who has not yet accepted the trusteeship may reject the trusteeship.  A designated trustee who does not accept the trusteeship within a reasonable time after knowing of the designation is considered to have rejected the trusteeship.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(3): A person designated as trustee, without accepting the trusteeship, may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(3)(a): act to preserve the trust property if, within a reasonable time after acting, the person sends a rejection of the trusteeship to the settlor or, if the settlor is dead or lacks capacity, to a qualified beneficiary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-701(3)(b): inspect or investigate trust property to determine potential liability under environmental or other law or for any other purpose.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-702 Trustee's bond.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-702(1): A trustee shall give bond to secure performance of the trustee's duties only if the court finds that a bond is needed to protect the interests of the beneficiaries or is required by the terms of the trust and the court has not dispensed with the requirement.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-702(2): The court may specify the amount of a bond, its liabilities, and whether sureties are necessary.  The court may modify or terminate a bond at any time.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-702(3): A regulated financial service institution qualified to do trust business in this state need not give bond, unless required by the terms of the trust.  The cost of any bond shall be borne by the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-702(4): Unless otherwise directed by the court, the cost of the bond is charged to the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703 Cotrustees.
------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(1): Cotrustees who are unable to reach a unanimous decision may act by majority decision.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(2): If a vacancy occurs in a cotrusteeship, the remaining cotrustees may act for the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(3): 75-12-112 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(4): If a cotrustee is unavailable to perform duties because of absence, illness, disqualification under other law, or other temporary incapacity, or if a cotrustee fails or refuses to act after reasonable notice, and prompt action is necessary to achieve the purposes of the trust or to avoid injury to the trust property, the remaining cotrustee or a majority of the remaining cotrustees may act for the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(5): A trustee may not delegate to a cotrustee the performance of a function the settlor intended the trustees to perform jointly as determined from the terms of the trust.  If one of the cotrustees is a regulated financial service institution qualified to do trust business in this state and the remaining cotrustees are individuals, a delegation by the individual cotrustees to the regulated financial service institution of the performance of trust investment functions shall be presumed to be in accordance with the settlor's intent unless the terms of the trust specifically provide otherwise.  Unless a delegation was irrevocable, a trustee may revoke a delegation previously made.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(6): (7) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(7): 75-12-112 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(7)(a): prevent a cotrustee from committing a serious breach of trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(7)(b): compel a cotrustee to redress a serious breach of trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-703(8): A dissenting trustee who joins in an action at the direction of the majority of the trustees and who notified any cotrustee of the dissent at or before the time of the action is not liable for the action unless the action is a serious breach of trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704 Vacancy in trusteeship -- Appointment of successor.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1): A vacancy in a trusteeship occurs if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1)(a): a person designated as trustee rejects the trusteeship;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1)(b): a person designated as trustee cannot be identified or does not exist;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1)(c): a trustee resigns;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1)(d): a trustee is disqualified or removed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1)(e): a trustee dies; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(1)(f): a guardian or conservator is appointed for an individual serving as trustee, unless otherwise provided in the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(2): If one or more cotrustees remain in office, a vacancy in a trusteeship need not be filled.  A vacancy in a trusteeship must be filled if the trust has no remaining trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(3): A vacancy in a trusteeship required to be filled must be filled in the following order of priority:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(3)(a): by a person designated in the terms of the trust to act as successor trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(3)(b): by a person appointed by unanimous agreement of the qualified beneficiaries; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(3)(c): by a person appointed by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(4): A vacancy in a trusteeship of a charitable trust that is required to be filled must be filled in the following order of priority:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(4)(a): by a person designated in the terms of the trust to act as successor trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(4)(b): by a person selected by the charitable organizations expressly designated to receive distributions under the terms of the trust if the attorney general concurs in the selection; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(4)(c): by a person appointed by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-704(5): Whether or not a vacancy in a trusteeship exists or is required to be filled, the court may appoint an additional trustee or special fiduciary whenever the court considers the appointment necessary for the administration of the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-705 Resignation of trustee.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-705(1): A trustee may resign:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-705(1)(a): upon at least 30 days' notice to the qualified beneficiaries, the settlor, if living, and all cotrustees; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-705(1)(b): with the approval of the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-705(2): In approving a resignation, the court may issue orders and impose conditions reasonably necessary for the protection of the trust property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-705(3): Any liability of a resigning trustee or of any sureties on the trustee's bond for acts or omissions of the trustee is not discharged or affected by the trustee's resignation.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706 Removal of trustee.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(1): The settlor, a cotrustee, or a qualified beneficiary may request the court to remove a trustee, or a trustee may be removed by the court on its own initiative.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(2): The court may remove a trustee if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(2)(a): the trustee has committed a serious breach of trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(2)(b): lack of cooperation among cotrustees substantially impairs the administration of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(2)(c): because of unfitness, unwillingness, or persistent failure of the trustee to administer the trust effectively, the court determines that removal of the trustee best serves the interests of the beneficiaries; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(2)(d): there has been a substantial change of circumstances or removal is requested by all of the qualified beneficiaries, the court finds that removal of the trustee best serves the interests of all of the beneficiaries and is not inconsistent with a material purpose of the trust, and a suitable cotrustee or successor trustee is available.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-706(3): 75-7-1001(2) Pending a final decision on a request to remove a trustee, or in lieu of or in addition to removing a trustee, the court may order appropriate relief under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-707 Delivery of property by former trustee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-707(1): Unless a cotrustee remains in office or the court otherwise orders, and until the trust property is delivered to a successor trustee or other person entitled to it, a trustee who has resigned or been removed has the duties of a trustee and the powers necessary to protect the trust property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-707(2): A trustee who has resigned or been removed shall proceed expeditiously to deliver the trust property within the trustee's possession to the cotrustee, successor trustee, or other person entitled to it.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-708 Compensation of trustee.
-------------------------------------------------------
If the terms of a trust do not specify the trustee's compensation, a trustee is entitled to compensation that is reasonable under the circumstances.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-709 Reimbursement of expenses.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-709(1): A trustee is entitled to be reimbursed out of the trust property, with interest as appropriate, for:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-709(1)(a): expenses that were properly incurred in the administration of the trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-709(1)(b): to the extent necessary to prevent unjust enrichment of the trust, expenses that were not properly incurred in the administration of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-709(2): An advance by the trustee of money for the protection of the trust gives rise to a lien against trust property to secure reimbursement with reasonable interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-801 Duty to administer trust.
--------------------------------------------------------
Upon acceptance of a trusteeship, the trustee shall administer the trust expeditiously and in good faith, in accordance with its terms and purposes and the interests of the beneficiaries, and in accordance with this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802 Duty of loyalty.
-----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(1): A trustee shall administer the trust solely in the interests of the beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(2): 75-7-1012; 75-7-1005; 75-7-1009 Subject to the rights of persons dealing with or assisting the trustee as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(2)(a): the transaction was authorized by the terms of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(2)(b): the transaction was approved by the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(2)(c): 75-7-1005 the beneficiary did not commence a judicial proceeding within the time allowed by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(2)(d): 75-7-1009 the beneficiary consented to the trustee's conduct, ratified the transaction, or released the trustee in compliance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(2)(e): the transaction involves a contract entered into or claim acquired by the trustee before the person became or contemplated becoming trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(3): A sale, encumbrance, or other transaction involving the investment or management of trust property is presumed to be affected by a conflict between personal and fiduciary interests if it is entered into by the trustee with:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(3)(a): the trustee's spouse;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(3)(b): the trustee's descendants, siblings, parents, or their spouses;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(3)(c): an agent of the trustee, including but not limited to an attorney, accountant, or financial advisor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(3)(d): a corporation or other person or enterprise in which the trustee, or a person that owns a significant interest in the trustee, has an interest that might affect the trustee's best judgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(4): A transaction between a trustee and a beneficiary that does not concern trust property but that occurs during the existence of the trust or while the trustee retains significant influence over the beneficiary and from which the trustee obtains an advantage is voidable by the beneficiary unless the trustee establishes that the transaction was fair to the beneficiary.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(5): A transaction not concerning trust property in which the trustee engages in the trustee's individual capacity involves a conflict between personal and fiduciary interests if the transaction concerns an opportunity properly belonging to the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(6): 75-7-901 An investment by a trustee in securities of an investment company or investment trust to which the trustee, or its affiliate, provides services in a capacity other than as trustee is not presumed to be affected by a conflict between personal and fiduciary interests if the investment complies with the prudent investor rule of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(7): In voting shares of stock or in exercising powers of control over similar interests in other forms of enterprise, the trustee shall act in the best interests of the beneficiaries.  If the trust is the sole owner of a corporation or other form of enterprise, the trustee shall elect or appoint directors or other managers who will manage the corporation or enterprise in the best interests of the beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8): This section does not preclude the following actions by the trustee:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(a): an agreement between the trustee and a beneficiary relating to the appointment or compensation of the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(b): payment of reasonable compensation to the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(c): a transaction between a trust and another trust, decedent's estate, conservatorship, or guardianship of which the trustee is a fiduciary or in which a beneficiary has an interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(d): a deposit of trust money in a regulated financial service institution operated by the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(e): an advance by the trustee of money for the protection of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(f): collecting, holding, and retaining trust assets received from a trustor until, in the judgment of the trustee, disposition of the assets should be made, even though the assets include an asset in which the trustee is personally interested;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(g): acquiring an undivided interest in a trust asset in which the trustee, in any trust capacity, holds an undivided interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(h): borrowing money to be repaid from the trust assets or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(i): advancing money to be repaid from the assets or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(j): employing persons, including attorneys, auditors, investment advisers, or agents, even if they are associated with the trustee:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(j)(i): to advise or assist the trustee in the performance of the trustee's administrative duties or perform any act of administration, whether or not discretionary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(j)(ii): to act without independent investigation upon their recommendations;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(k): if a governing instrument or order requires or authorizes investment in United States government obligations, investing in those obligations, either directly or in the form of securities or other interests, in any open-end or closed-end management type investment company or investment trust registered under the provisions of the Investment Company Act of 1940, 15 U.S.C. Sections 80a-1 through 80a-64 if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(k)(i): the portfolio of the investment company or investment trust is limited to United States government obligations, and repurchase agreements are fully collateralized by United States government obligations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(8)(k)(ii): the investment company or investment trust takes delivery of the collateral for any repurchase agreement either directly or through an authorized custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-802(9): The court may appoint a special fiduciary to make a decision with respect to any proposed transaction that might violate this section if entered into by the trustee.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-803 Impartiality.
--------------------------------------------
If a trust has two or more beneficiaries, the trustee shall act impartially in investing, managing, and distributing the trust property, giving due regard to the beneficiaries' respective interests.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-804 Prudent administration.
------------------------------------------------------
A trustee shall administer the trust as a prudent person would, by considering the purposes, terms, distributional requirements, and other circumstances of the trust.  In satisfying this standard, the trustee shall exercise reasonable care, skill, and caution.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-805 Costs of administration.
-------------------------------------------------------
In administering a trust, the trustee may incur only costs that are reasonable in relation to the trust property, the purposes of the trust, and the skills of the trustee.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-806 Trustee's skills.
------------------------------------------------
A trustee who is named trustee in reliance upon the trustee's representation that the trustee has special skills or expertise, shall use those special skills or expertise.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-807 Control and protection of trust property.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
A trustee shall take reasonable steps to take control of and protect the trust property.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-808 Recordkeeping and identification of trust property.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-808(1): A trustee shall keep adequate records of the administration of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-808(2): A trustee shall keep trust property separate from the trustee's own property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-808(3): (4) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-808(4): If the trustee maintains records clearly indicating the respective interests, a trustee may invest as a whole the property of two or more separate trusts.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-809 Enforcement and defense of claims.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
A trustee shall take reasonable steps to enforce claims of the trust and to defend claims against the trust.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-810 Collecting trust property.
---------------------------------------------------------
A trustee shall take reasonable steps to compel a former trustee or other person to deliver trust property to the trustee, and to redress a breach of trust known to the trustee to have been committed by a former trustee, unless the terms of the trust provide otherwise.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811 Duty to inform and report.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(1): Except to the extent the terms of the trust provide otherwise, a trustee shall keep the qualified beneficiaries of the trust reasonably informed about the administration of the trust and of the material facts necessary for them to protect their interests.  Unless unreasonable under the circumstances, and unless otherwise provided by the terms of the trust a trustee shall promptly respond to a qualified beneficiary's request for information related to the administration of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(2): (3) Except to the extent the terms of the trust provide otherwise, a trustee:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(2)(a): upon request of a qualified beneficiary, shall promptly furnish to the beneficiary a copy of the portions of the trust instrument which describe or affect the beneficiary's interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(2)(b): within 60 days after accepting a trusteeship, shall notify the qualified beneficiaries of the acceptance and of the trustee's name, address, and telephone number;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(2)(c): (3) within 60 days after the date the trustee acquires knowledge of the creation of an irrevocable trust, or the date the trustee acquires knowledge that a formerly revocable trust has become irrevocable, whether by the death of the settlor or otherwise, shall notify the qualified beneficiaries of the trust's existence, of the identity of the settlor or settlors, of the right to request a copy of the trust instrument, and of the right to a trustee's report as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(2)(d): shall notify the qualified beneficiaries in advance of any change in the method or rate of the trustee's compensation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(3): A trustee shall send to the qualified beneficiaries who request it, at least annually and at the termination of the trust, a report of the trust property, liabilities, receipts, and disbursements, including the amount of the trustee's compensation or a fee schedule or other writing showing how the trustee's compensation was determined, a listing of the trust assets and, if feasible, their respective market values.  Upon a vacancy in a trusteeship, unless a cotrustee remains in office, a report must be sent to the qualified beneficiaries by the former trustee, unless the terms of the trust provide otherwise.  A personal representative, conservator, or guardian may send the qualified beneficiaries a report on behalf of a deceased or incapacitated trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-811(4): A qualified beneficiary may waive the right to a trustee's report or other information otherwise required to be furnished under this section.  A beneficiary, with respect to future reports and other information, may withdraw a waiver previously given.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812 Discretionary powers -- Tax savings.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
