Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(1): Notwithstanding the breadth of discretion granted to a trustee in the terms of the trust, including the use of such terms as "absolute," "sole," or "uncontrolled," the trustee shall exercise a discretionary power in good faith and in accordance with the terms and purposes of the trust and the interests of the beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(2): (4) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(2)(a): a person other than a settlor who is a beneficiary and trustee of a trust that confers on the trustee a power to make discretionary distributions to or for the trustee's personal benefit may exercise the power only in accordance with an ascertainable standard relating to the trustee's individual health, education, support, or maintenance within the meaning of Subsection 2041(b)(1)(A) or 2514(c)(1) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as in effect on May 1, 2004; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(2)(b): a trustee may not exercise a power to make discretionary distributions to satisfy a legal obligation of support that the trustee personally owes another person.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(3): (2) A power whose exercise is limited or prohibited by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(4): (2) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(4)(a): a power held by the settlor's spouse who is the trustee of a trust for which a marital deduction, as defined in Subsection 2056(b)(5) or 2523(e) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as in effect on May 1, 2004, was previously allowed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(4)(b): any trust during any period that the trust may be revoked or amended by its settlor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-812(4)(c): a trust if contributions to the trust qualify for the annual exclusion under Subsection 2503(c) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as in effect on May 1, 2004.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813 General powers of trustee.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(1): A trustee, without authorization by the court, may exercise:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(1)(a): powers conferred by the terms of the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(1)(b): except as limited by the terms of the trust:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(1)(b)(i): all powers over the trust property which an unmarried competent owner has over individually owned property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(1)(b)(ii): any other powers appropriate to achieve the proper investment, management, and distribution of the trust property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(1)(b)(iii): any other powers conferred by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-813(2): The exercise of a power is subject to the fiduciary duties prescribed by this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814 Specific powers of trustee.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1): 75-7-813 Without limiting the authority conferred by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(a): collect trust property and accept or reject additions to the trust property from a settlor or any other person;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(b): acquire or sell property, for cash or on credit, at public or private sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(c): exchange, partition, or otherwise change the character of trust property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(d): deposit trust money in an account in a regulated financial service institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(e): borrow money, with or without security from any financial institution, including a financial institution that is serving as a trustee or one of its affiliates, and mortgage or pledge trust property for a period within or extending beyond the duration of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(f): with respect to an interest in a proprietorship, partnership, limited liability company, business trust, corporation, or other form of business or enterprise, continue the business or other enterprise and take any action that may be taken by shareholders, members, or property owners, including merging, dissolving, or otherwise changing the form of business organization or contributing additional capital;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(g): with respect to stocks or other securities, exercise the rights of an absolute owner, including the right to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(g)(i): vote, or give proxies to vote, with or without power of substitution, or enter into or continue a voting trust agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(g)(ii): hold a security in the name of a nominee or in other form without disclosure of the trust so that title may pass by delivery;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(g)(iii): pay calls, assessments, and other sums chargeable or accruing against the securities, and sell or exercise stock subscription or conversion rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(g)(iv): deposit the securities with a depositary or other regulated financial service institution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(h): with respect to an interest in real property, construct, or make ordinary or extraordinary repairs to, alterations to, or improvements in, buildings or other structures, demolish improvements, raze existing or erect new party walls or buildings, subdivide or develop land, dedicate land to public use or grant public or private easements, and make or vacate plats and adjust boundaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(i): enter into a lease for any purpose as lessor or lessee, including a lease or other arrangement for exploration and removal of natural resources, with or without the option to purchase or renew, for a period within or extending beyond the duration of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(j): grant an option involving a sale, lease, or other disposition of trust property or acquire an option for the acquisition of property, including an option exercisable beyond the duration of the trust, and exercise an option so acquired;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(k): insure the property of the trust against damage or loss and insure the trustee, the trustee's agents, and beneficiaries against liability arising from the administration of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(l): abandon or decline to administer property of no value or of insufficient value to justify its collection or continued administration;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(m): with respect to possible liability for violation of environmental law:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(m)(i): inspect or investigate property the trustee holds or has been asked to hold, or property owned or operated by an organization in which the trustee holds or has been asked to hold an interest, for the purpose of determining the application of environmental law with respect to the property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(m)(ii): take action to prevent, abate, or otherwise remedy any actual or potential violation of any environmental law affecting property held directly or indirectly by the trustee, whether taken before or after the assertion of a claim or the initiation of governmental enforcement;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(m)(iii): decline to accept property into trust or disclaim any power with respect to property that is or may be burdened with liability for violation of environmental law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(m)(iv): compromise claims against the trust which may be asserted for an alleged violation of environmental law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(m)(v): pay the expense of any inspection, review, abatement, or remedial action to comply with environmental law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(n): pay or contest any claim, settle a claim by or against the trust, and release, in whole or in part, a claim belonging to the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(o): pay taxes, assessments, compensation of the trustee and of employees and agents of the trust, and other expenses incurred in the administration of the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(p): exercise elections with respect to federal, state, and local taxes;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(q): select a mode of payment under any employee benefit or retirement plan, annuity, or life insurance payable to the trustee, exercise rights thereunder, including exercise of the right to indemnification for expenses and against liabilities, and take appropriate action to collect the proceeds;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(r): make loans out of trust property, including loans to a beneficiary on terms and conditions the trustee considers to be fair and reasonable under the circumstances, and the trustee has a lien on future distributions for repayment of those loans;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(s): pledge trust property to guarantee loans made by others to the beneficiary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(t): appoint a trustee to act in another jurisdiction with respect to trust property located in the other jurisdiction, confer upon the appointed trustee all of the powers and duties of the appointing trustee, require that the appointed trustee furnish security, and remove any trustee so appointed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(u): pay an amount distributable to a beneficiary who is under a legal disability or who the trustee reasonably believes is incapacitated, by paying it directly to the beneficiary or applying it for the beneficiary's benefit, or by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(u)(i): paying it to the beneficiary's conservator or, if the beneficiary does not have a conservator, the beneficiary's guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(u)(ii): paying it to the beneficiary's custodian under Title 75A, Chapter 8, Uniform Transfers to Minors Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(u)(iii): if the trustee does not know of a conservator, guardian, custodian, or custodial trustee, paying it to an adult relative or other person having legal or physical care or custody of the beneficiary, to be expended on the beneficiary's behalf; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(u)(iv): managing it as a separate fund on the beneficiary's behalf, subject to the beneficiary's continuing right to withdraw the distribution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(v): on distribution of trust property or the division or termination of a trust, make distributions in divided or undivided interests, allocate particular assets in proportionate or disproportionate shares, value the trust property for those purposes, and adjust for resulting differences in valuation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(w): resolve a dispute concerning the interpretation of the trust or its administration by mediation, arbitration, or other procedure for alternative dispute resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(x): prosecute or defend an action, claim, or judicial proceeding in any jurisdiction to protect trust property and the trustee in the performance of the trustee's duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(y): sign and deliver contracts and other instruments that are useful to achieve or facilitate the exercise of the trustee's powers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(1)(z): on termination of the trust, exercise the powers appropriate to finalize the administration of the trust and distribute the trust property to the persons entitled to it.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2): A trustee may delegate investment and management functions that a prudent trustee of comparable skills could properly delegate under the circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2)(a): The trustee shall exercise reasonable care, skill, and caution in:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2)(a)(i): selecting the agent;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2)(a)(ii): establishing the scope and terms of the delegation consistent with the purposes of the trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2)(a)(iii): periodically reviewing the agent's actions to monitor the agent's performance and compliance with the terms of the delegation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2)(b): In performing a delegated function, an agent has a duty to the trust to exercise reasonable care to comply with the terms of the delegation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(2)(c): A trustee who complies with the requirements of this Subsection (2) is not liable to the beneficiaries or to the trust for the decisions or actions of the agent to whom the function was delegated.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-814(3): The trustee may exercise the powers set forth in this section and in the trust either in the name of the trust or in the name of the trustee as trustee, specifically including the right to take title, to encumber or convey assets, including real property, in the name of the trust.  This Subsection (3) applies to a trustee's exercise of trust powers.  After May 11, 2010, for recording purposes, the name of the trustee, the address of the trustee, and the name and date of the trust, shall be included on all recorded documents affecting real property to which the trust is a party in interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-815 Distribution upon termination.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-815(1): Upon termination or partial termination of a trust, the trustee may send to the beneficiaries a proposal for distribution.  The right of any beneficiary to object to the proposed distribution terminates if the beneficiary does not notify the trustee of an objection within 30 days after the proposal was sent but only if the proposal informed the beneficiary of the right to object and of the time allowed for objection.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-815(2): Upon the occurrence of an event terminating or partially terminating a trust, the trustee shall proceed expeditiously to distribute the trust property to the persons entitled to it, subject to the right of the trustee to retain a reasonable reserve for the payment of debts, expenses, and taxes.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-815(3): A release by a beneficiary of a trustee from liability for breach of trust is invalid to the extent:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-815(3)(a): it was induced by improper conduct of the trustee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-815(3)(b): the beneficiary, at the time of the release, did not know or had no reason to know of the beneficiary's rights or of the material facts relating to the breach.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816 Recitals when title to real property is in trust -- Failure.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(1): When title to real property is granted to a person as trustee, the terms of the trust may be given either:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(1)(a): in the deed of transfer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(1)(b): in an instrument signed by the grantor and recorded in the same office as the grant to the trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(2): If the terms of the trust are not made public as required in Subsection (1), a conveyance from the trustee is absolute in favor of purchasers for value who take the property without notice of the terms of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(3): The terms of the trust recited in the deed of transfer or the instrument recorded under Subsection (1)(b) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(3)(a): the name of the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(3)(b): the address of the trustee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(3)(c): the name and date of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-816(4): 75B-1-302 Any real property titled in a trust which has a restriction on transfer described in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-817 Marital deduction formulas -- Trusts.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-817(1): For estates of decedents dying after December 31, 1981, where a decedent's trust executed before September 13, 1981, contains a formula expressly providing that the decedent's spouse is to receive the maximum amount of property qualifying for the marital deduction allowable by federal law, this formula shall be construed as referring to the unlimited marital deduction allowable by federal law as amended by Section 403(a) of the Economic Recovery Tax Act of 1981.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-817(2): (1); (1) The intention of a trustor as expressed in the trust shall control the legal effect of any dispositions made by it for purposes of construing Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-901 Prudent investor rule.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-901(1): (2) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-901(2): The prudent investor rule is a default rule and may be expanded, restricted, eliminated, or otherwise altered by the provisions of a trust.  A trustee is not liable to a beneficiary to the extent that the trustee acted in reasonable reliance on the provisions of the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902 Standard of care -- Portfolio strategy -- Risk and return objectives.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(1): A trustee shall invest and manage trust assets as a prudent investor would, by considering the purposes, terms, distribution requirements, and other circumstances of the trust.  In satisfying this standard, the trustee shall exercise reasonable care, skill, and caution.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(2): A trustee's investment and management decisions respecting individual assets must be evaluated not in isolation but in the context of the trust portfolio as a whole and as a part of an overall investment strategy having risk and return objectives reasonably suited to the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3): Among circumstances that a trustee shall consider in investing and managing trust assets are the following which may be relevant to the trust or its beneficiaries:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(a): general economic conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(b): the possible effect of inflation or deflation;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(c): the expected tax consequences of investment decisions or strategies;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(d): the role that each investment or course of action plays within the overall trust portfolio, which may include financial assets, interests in closely held enterprises, tangible and intangible personal property, and real property;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(e): the expected total return from income and the appreciation of capital;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(f): other resources of the beneficiaries;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(g): needs for liquidity, regularity of income, and preservation or appreciation of capital; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(3)(h): an asset's special relationship or special value, if any, to the purposes of the trust or to one or more of the beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(4): A trustee shall make a reasonable effort to verify facts relevant to the investment and management of trust assets.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-902(5): A trustee may invest in any kind of property or type of investment consistent with the standards of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-903 Diversification.
-----------------------------------------------
A trustee shall diversify the investments of the trust unless the trustee reasonably determines that, because of special circumstances, the purposes of the trust are better served without diversifying.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-904 Duties at inception of trusteeship.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Within a reasonable time after accepting a trusteeship or receiving trust assets, a trustee shall review the trust assets and make and implement decisions concerning the retention and disposition of assets, in order to bring the trust portfolio into compliance with the purposes, terms, distribution requirements, and other circumstances of the trust, and with the requirements of this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-905 Reviewing compliance.
----------------------------------------------------
Compliance with the prudent investor rule is determined in light of the facts and circumstances existing at the time of a trustee's decision or action and not by hindsight.  This section does not require a specific outcome in investing.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906 Investment direction.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1): (2) For purposes of this section, "investment direction" means a direction that is binding on the trustee, except for an investment direction given by a settlor as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1)(a): retention;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1)(b): purchase;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1)(c): sale;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1)(d): exchange;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1)(e): tender; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(1)(f): any other transaction affecting ownership in the investment.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(2)(a): During the time period that a trust is revocable, the trustee may follow any investment direction of the settlor, including an investment direction that:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(2)(a)(i): is manifestly contrary to the terms of the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(2)(a)(ii): seriously breaches a fiduciary duty to the beneficiaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(2)(b): (2)(a) The trustee is not liable for any loss resulting from following an investment direction described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(3): If the terms of a trust authorize a person to give investment direction to the trustee, the person authorized to give investment direction:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(3)(a): is presumptively a fiduciary only with respect to an investment direction that the person gives to the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(3)(b): is required to act in good faith with regard to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(3)(b)(i): the purposes of the trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(3)(b)(ii): the interests of the beneficiaries; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(3)(c): is liable for any loss that results from breach of the fiduciary duty only with respect to an investment direction that the person gives to the trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(4): (4)(a) Except in cases of willful misconduct or gross negligence, a trustee is not liable for any loss that results from following an investment direction if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(4)(a): the terms of a trust authorizes a person to give the investment direction to the trustee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(4)(b): (4)(a) the trustee acts in accordance with the investment direction given by a person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5): If the terms of a trust require another person's approval or consent to an investment decision of the trustee:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(a): the person from whom approval or consent is required:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(a)(i): is presumptively a fiduciary;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(a)(ii): is required to act in good faith with regard to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(a)(ii)(A): the purposes of the trust; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(a)(ii)(B): the interests of the beneficiaries; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(a)(iii): is liable for any loss that results from breach of the fiduciary duty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-906(5)(b): except in cases of willful misconduct or gross negligence, the trustee is not liable for any loss resulting from any act not taken as a result of the person's failure to respond to a request for approval or consent.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-907 Language invoking standard of chapter.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
The following terms or comparable language in the provisions of a trust, unless otherwise limited or modified, authorizes any investment or strategy permitted under this chapter: "investments permissible by law for investment of trust funds," "legal investments," "authorized investments," "using the judgment and care under the circumstances then prevailing that persons of prudence, discretion, and intelligence exercise in the management of their own affairs, not in regard to speculation but in regard to the permanent disposition of their funds, considering the probable income as well as the probable safety of their capital," "prudent man rule," "prudent trustee rule," "prudent person rule," and "prudent investor rule."

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001 Remedies for breach of trust.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(1): A violation by a trustee of a duty the trustee owes to a beneficiary is a breach of trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2): 75-7-706; 75-7-1012 To remedy a breach of trust that has occurred or may occur, the court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(a): compel the trustee to perform the trustee's duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(b): enjoin the trustee from committing a breach of trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(c): compel the trustee to redress a breach of trust by paying money, restoring property, or other means;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(d): order a trustee to account;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(e): appoint a special fiduciary to take possession of the trust property and administer the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(f): suspend the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(g): 75-7-706 remove the trustee as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(h): reduce or deny compensation to the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(i): 75-7-1012 subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1001(2)(j): order any other appropriate relief.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1002 Damages for breach of trust.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1002(1): A trustee who commits a breach of trust is liable to the beneficiaries affected for the greater of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1002(1)(a): the amount required to restore the value of the trust property and trust distributions to what they would have been had the breach not occurred; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1002(1)(b): the profit the trustee made by reason of the breach.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1002(2): (2) Except as otherwise provided in this Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1003 Damages in absence of breach.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1003(1): A trustee is accountable to an affected beneficiary for any profit made by the trustee arising from the administration of the trust, even absent a breach of trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1003(2): Absent a breach of trust, a trustee is not liable to a beneficiary for a loss or depreciation in the value of trust property or for not having made a profit.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1004 Attorney's fees and costs.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1004(1): In a judicial proceeding involving the administration of a trust, the court may, as justice and equity may require, award costs and expenses, including reasonable attorney's fees, to any party, to be paid by another party or from the trust that is the subject of the controversy.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1004(2): If a trustee defends or prosecutes any proceeding in good faith, whether successful or not, the trustee is entitled to receive from the trust the necessary expenses and disbursements, including reasonable attorney's fees, incurred.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005 Limitation of action against trustee.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(1): A beneficiary may not commence a proceeding against a trustee for breach of trust more than six months after the date that the beneficiary or a person who may represent and bind the beneficiary was sent a report that adequately disclosed the existence of a potential claim for breach of trust and informed the beneficiary of the time allowed for commencing a proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(2): A report adequately discloses the existence of a potential claim for breach of trust if it provides sufficient information so that the beneficiary or representative knows of the potential claim or should have inquired into its existence.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(3): (1) If Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(3)(a): the removal, resignation, or death of the trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(3)(b): the termination of the beneficiary's interest in the trust; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(3)(c): the termination of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1005(4): This section does not preclude an action to recover for fraud or misrepresentation related to the report.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1006 Reliance on trust instrument.
-------------------------------------------------------------
A trustee who acts in reasonable reliance on the terms of the trust as expressed in the trust instrument is not liable to a beneficiary for a breach of trust to the extent the breach resulted from the reliance.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1007 Event affecting administration or distribution.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If the happening of an event, including marriage, divorce, performance of educational requirements, or death, affects the administration or distribution of a trust, a trustee is not liable for a loss resulting from the trustee's lack of knowledge or lack of notice.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1008 Exculpation of trustee.
-------------------------------------------------------
A term of a trust relieving a trustee of liability for breach of trust is unenforceable to the extent that it:Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1008(1): relieves the trustee of liability for breach of trust committed in bad faith or with reckless indifference to the purposes of the trust or the interests of the beneficiaries; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1008(2): was inserted by the trustee or fiduciary without disclosure of its existence and contents.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1009 Beneficiary's consent, release, or ratification.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
A trustee is not liable to a beneficiary for breach of trust if the beneficiary, while having capacity, consented to the conduct constituting the breach, released the trustee from liability for the breach, or ratified the transaction constituting the breach, unless at the time of the consent, release, or ratification, the beneficiary did not know of the beneficiary's rights or of the material facts relating to the breach.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010 Limitation on personal liability of trustee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010(1): Except as otherwise provided in the contract, a trustee is not personally liable on a contract properly entered into in the trustee's fiduciary capacity in the course of administering the trust if the trustee in the contract disclosed the fiduciary capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010(2): A trustee is personally liable for torts committed in the course of administering a trust, or for obligations arising from ownership or control of trust property, including liability for violation of environmental law, only if the trustee is personally at fault.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010(3): A claim based on a contract entered into by a trustee in the trustee's fiduciary capacity, on an obligation arising from ownership or control of trust property, or on a tort committed in the course of administering a trust, may be asserted in a judicial proceeding against the trustee in the trustee's fiduciary capacity, whether or not the trustee is personally liable for the claim.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010(4): The question of liability as between the trust estate and the trustee individually may be determined in a proceeding for accounting, surcharge, or indemnification or other appropriate proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010(5): Whenever an instrument creating a trust reserves to the settlor, or vests in an advisory or investment committee, or in any other person or persons, including one or more cotrustees to the exclusion of the trustee or to the exclusion of one or more of several trustees, authority to direct the making or retention of any investment, the excluded trustee or trustees shall not be liable, either individually or as a fiduciary, for any loss resulting from the making or retention of any investment pursuant to such direction.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1010(6): In the absence of actual knowledge or information which would cause a reasonable trustee to inquire further, no trustee shall be liable for failure to take necessary steps to compel the redress of any breach of trust or fiduciary duty by any predecessor personal representative, trustee, or other fiduciary.  The provisions of this section shall not be construed to limit the fiduciary liability of any trustee for his own acts or omissions with respect to the trust estate.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1011 Interest as general partner.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1011(1): (3); Title 48, Chapter 2e, Utah Uniform Limited Partnership Act Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1011(2): (3) Except as otherwise provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1011(3): The immunity provided by this section does not apply if an interest in the partnership is held by the trustee in a capacity other than that of trustee or is held by the trustee's spouse or one or more of the trustee's descendants, siblings, or parents, or the spouse of any of them.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1011(4): If the trustee of a revocable trust holds an interest as a general partner, the settlor is personally liable for contracts and other obligations of the partnership as if the settlor were a general partner.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1012 Protection of person dealing with trustee.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1012(1): A person other than a beneficiary who in good faith assists a trustee, or who in good faith and for value deals with a trustee, without knowledge that the trustee is exceeding or improperly exercising the trustee's powers is protected from liability as if the trustee properly exercised the power.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1012(2): A person other than a beneficiary who in good faith deals with a trustee is not required to inquire into the extent of the trustee's powers or the propriety of their exercise.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1012(3): A person who in good faith delivers assets to a trustee need not ensure their proper application.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1012(4): A person other than a beneficiary who in good faith assists a former trustee, or who in good faith and for value deals with a former trustee, without knowledge that the trusteeship has terminated is protected from liability as if the former trustee were still a trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1012(5): Comparable protective provisions of other laws relating to commercial transactions or transfer of securities by fiduciaries prevail over the protection provided by this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013 Certification of trust.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1): Instead of furnishing a copy of the trust instrument to a person other than a beneficiary, the trustee may furnish to the person a certification of trust containing the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(a): that the trust exists and the date the trust instrument was executed;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(b): the identity of the settlor;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(c): the identity and address of the currently acting trustee;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(d): the powers of the trustee in the pending transaction;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(e): the revocability or irrevocability of the trust and the identity of any person holding a power to revoke the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(f): the authority of cotrustees to sign or otherwise authenticate and whether all or less than all are required in order to exercise powers of the trustee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(1)(g): the name in which title to trust property may be taken.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(2): A certification of trust may be signed or otherwise authenticated by any trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(3): A certification of trust must state that the trust has not been revoked, modified, or amended in any manner that would cause the representations contained in the certification of trust to be incorrect.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(4): A certification of trust need not contain the dispositive terms of a trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(5): A recipient of a certification of trust may require the trustee to furnish copies of those excerpts from the original trust instrument and later amendments which designate the trustee and confer upon the trustee the power to act in the pending transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(6): A person who acts in reliance upon a certification of trust without knowledge that the representations contained in it are incorrect is not liable to any person for acting and may assume without inquiry the existence of the facts contained in the certification.  Knowledge of the terms of the trust may not be inferred solely from the fact that a copy of all or part of the trust instrument is held by the person relying upon the certification.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(7): A person who in good faith enters into a transaction in reliance upon a certification of trust may enforce the transaction against the trust property as if the representations contained in the certification were correct.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(8): A person making a demand for the trust instrument in addition to a certification of trust or excerpts is liable for costs, expenses, attorney fees, and damages if the court determines that the person did not act in good faith in demanding the trust instrument.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1013(9): This section does not limit the right of a person to obtain a copy of the trust instrument in a judicial proceeding concerning the trust.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1101 Uniformity of application and construction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this chapter, consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1102 Electronic records and signatures.
------------------------------------------------------------------
The provisions of this chapter governing the legal effect, validity, or enforceability of electronic records or electronic signatures, and of contracts formed or performed with the use of such records or signatures, conform to the requirements of Section 102 of the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act (15 U.S.C. Sec. 7002) and supersede, modify, and limit the requirements of the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103 Application to existing relationships.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(1): Except as otherwise provided, this chapter applies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(1)(a): all trusts created before, on, or after July 1, 2004;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(1)(b): all judicial proceedings concerning trusts commenced on or after July 1, 2004; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(1)(c): judicial proceedings concerning trusts commenced before July 1, 2004 unless the court finds that application of a particular provision of this chapter would substantially interfere with the effective conduct of the judicial proceedings or prejudice the rights of the parties, in which case the particular provision of this chapter does not apply and the superseded section will apply.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(2): Any rule of construction or presumption provided in this chapter applies to trust instruments executed before July 1, 2004 unless there is a clear indication of a contrary intent in the terms of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(3): An act done before July 1, 2004 is not affected by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1103(4): If a right is acquired, extinguished, or barred upon the expiration of a prescribed period that has commenced to run under any other statute before July 1, 2004, that statute continues to apply to the right even if it has been repealed or superseded.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1201 Foreign trustees.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1201(1): A foreign corporate trustee is required to qualify as a foreign corporation doing business in this state if it maintains the principal place of administration of any trust within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1201(2): A foreign corporate cotrustee is not required to qualify in this state solely because its cotrustee maintains the principal place of administration in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1201(3): Unless otherwise doing business in this state, local qualification by a foreign corporate trustee is not required in order for the trustee to receive distribution from a local estate or to hold, invest in, manage, or acquire property located in this state, or maintain litigation if the state of the principal place of business of the foreign corporate trustee provides substantially similar provisions applicable to trustees from this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1201(4): Local qualification by a foreign trustee other than a corporation is not required in order for the trustee to receive distribution from a local estate or to hold, invest in, manage, or acquire property located in this state or maintain litigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-7-1201(5): Nothing in this section affects a determination of what other acts require qualification as doing business in this state.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 75 - Chapter 8 - Effective Date
***********************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101 Time of taking effect -- Provisions for transition.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(1): This code takes effect on July 1, 1977.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(2): Except as provided elsewhere in this code, on the effective date of this code:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(2)(a): This code applies to any wills of decedents dying thereafter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(2)(b): The code applies to any proceedings in court then pending or thereafter commenced regardless of the time of the death of decedent except to the extent that in the opinion of the court the former procedure should be made applicable in a particular case in the interest of justice or because of infeasibility of application of the procedure of this code.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(2)(c): Every personal representative including a person administering an estate of a minor or incompetent holding an appointment on that date, continues to hold the appointment but has only the powers conferred by this code and is subject to the duties imposed with respect to any act occurring or done thereafter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(2)(d): An act done before the effective date in any proceeding and any accrued right is not impaired by this code. If a right is acquired, extinguished or barred upon the expiration of a prescribed period of time which has commenced to run by the provisions of any statute before the effective date, the provisions shall remain in force with respect to that right.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-8-101(2)(e): Any rule of construction or presumption provided in this code applies to instruments executed and multiple-party accounts opened before the effective date unless there is a clear indication of a contrary intent.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 75 - Chapter 12 - Uniform Directed Trust Act
************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Uniform Directed Trust Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(1): "Breach of trust" includes a violation by a trust director or trustee of a duty imposed on the director or trustee by the terms of the trust, this chapter, or the law of this state other than this chapter pertaining to trusts.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(2): "Directed trust" means a trust for which the terms of the trust grant a power of direction.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(3): "Directed trustee" means a trustee that is subject to a trust director's power of direction.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(4): "Person" means an individual, estate, business or nonprofit entity, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency, instrumentality, or other legal entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(5): 75-12-105(2)
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(5)(a): "Power of direction" means a power over a trust granted to a person by the terms of the trust to the extent the power is exercisable while the person is not serving as a trustee.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(5)(b): "Power of direction" includes a power over the investment, management, or distribution of trust property or other matters of trust administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(5)(c): 75-12-105(2) "Power of direction" does not include the powers described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(6): 75-7-103 "Settlor" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(7): "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, or any territory or insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8): (8)(b); 75-7-110 "Terms of a trust" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(a): (8)(b) subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(a)(i): expressed in the trust instrument; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(a)(ii): established by other evidence that would be admissible in a judicial proceeding; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(b): 75-7-110 the trust's provisions as established, determined, or amended by:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(b)(i): a trustee or trust director in accordance with applicable law;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(b)(ii): a court order; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(8)(b)(iii): 75-7-110 a nonjudicial settlement agreement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(9): "Trust director" means a person that is granted a power of direction by the terms of a trust to the extent the power is exercisable while the person is not serving as a trustee, regardless of whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(9)(a): the terms of the trust refer to the person as a trust director; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(9)(b): the person is a beneficiary or settlor of the trust.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-102(10): "Trustee" includes an original, additional, and successor trustee, and a cotrustee.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103 Application -- Principal place of administration.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(1): This chapter applies to a trust, whenever created, that has the trust's principal place of administration in this state, subject to the following rules:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(1)(a): if the trust was created before May 14, 2019, this chapter applies only to a decision or action occurring on or after May 14, 2019; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(1)(b): if the principal place of administration of the trust is changed to this state on or after May 14, 2019, this chapter applies only to a decision or action occurring on or after the date of the change.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(2): Without precluding other means to establish a sufficient connection with the designated jurisdiction in a directed trust, the terms of the trust that designate the principal place of administration of the trust are valid and controlling if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(2)(a): a trustee's principal place of business is located in, or a trustee is a resident of, the designated jurisdiction;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(2)(b): a trust director's principal place of business is located in, or a trust director is a resident of, the designated jurisdiction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-103(2)(c): all or part of the administration occurs in the designated jurisdiction.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-104 Common law and principles of equity.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
The common law and principles of equity supplement this chapter, except to the extent modified by this chapter or the law of this state other than this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105 Exclusions.
-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(1): As used in this section, "power of appointment" means a power that enables a person acting in a nonfiduciary capacity to designate a recipient of an ownership interest in, or another power of appointment over, trust property.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2): 75-7-301; 75-7-305 This chapter does not apply to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(a): a power of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(b): a power to appoint or remove a trustee or trust director;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(c): a power of a settlor over a trust to the extent the settlor has a power to revoke the trust;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(d): 75-7-301; 75-7-305 a power of a beneficiary over a trust to the extent the exercise or nonexercise of the power affects the beneficial interest of:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(d)(i): the beneficiary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(d)(ii): 75-7-301; 75-7-305 another beneficiary represented by the beneficiary under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(e): power over a trust if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(e)(i): the terms of the trust provide that the power is held in a nonfiduciary capacity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(2)(e)(ii): the power must be held in a nonfiduciary capacity to achieve the settlor's tax objectives under the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended, and any related Internal Revenue Service regulations.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-105(3): Unless the terms of a trust provide otherwise, a power granted to a person to designate a recipient of an ownership interest in, or power of appointment over, trust property that is exercisable while the person is not serving as trustee is a power of appointment and not a power of direction.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-106 Powers of trust director.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-106(1): 75-12-107 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-106(2): (1) Unless the terms of a trust provide otherwise:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-106(2)(a): (1) a trust director may exercise any further power appropriate to the exercise or nonexercise of a power of direction granted to the director under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-106(2)(b): trust directors with joint powers shall act by majority decision.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-107 Limitations on trust director.
--------------------------------------------------------------
A trust director is subject to the same rules as a trustee in a like position and under similar circumstances in the exercise or nonexercise of a power of direction or further power under SubsectionUtah Code Annotated § 75-12-107(1): a payback provision in the terms of a trust necessary to comply with the Medicaid reimbursement requirements in Section 1917 of the Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C. Sec. 1396p(d)(4)(A), as amended, and any related regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-107(2): a charitable interest in the trust, including notice regarding the interest to the attorney general.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108 Duty and liability of trust director.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(1): (2); 75-12-106(2)(a) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(1)(a): a trust director has the same fiduciary duty and liability in the exercise or nonexercise of the power:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(1)(a)(i): if the power is held individually, as a sole trustee in a like position and under similar circumstances; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(1)(a)(ii): if the power is held jointly with a trustee or another trust director, as a cotrustee in a like position and under similar circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(1)(b): the terms of the trust may vary the director's duty or liability to the same extent the terms of the trust could vary the duty or liability of a trustee in a like position and under similar circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(2): Unless the terms of a trust provide otherwise, if a trust director is licensed, certified, or otherwise authorized or permitted by law other than this chapter to provide health care in the ordinary course of the director's business or practice of a profession, to the extent the director acts in that capacity, the director has no duty or liability under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-108(3): The terms of a trust may impose a duty or liability on a trust director in addition to the duties and liability described in this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109 Duty and liability of directed trustee.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(1): (2); 75-12-106(2)(a) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(2): 75-12-106(2)(a) A directed trustee may not comply with a trust director's exercise or nonexercise of a power of direction or further power under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(3): An exercise of a power of direction under which a trust director may release a trustee or another trust director from liability for breach of trust is not effective if:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(3)(a): the breach involved the trustee's or other director's willful misconduct;
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(3)(b): the release was induced by improper conduct of the trustee or other director in procuring the release; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(3)(c): at the time of the release, the director did not know the material facts relating to the breach.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(4): A directed trustee that has reasonable doubt about the directed trustee's duty under this section may petition the court for instructions.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-109(5): The terms of a trust may impose a duty or liability on a directed trustee in addition to the duties and liabilities under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110 Duty to provide information to trust director or trustee.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(1): 75-12-111 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(1)(a): the powers or duties of the trustee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(1)(b): the powers or duties of the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(2): 75-12-111 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(2)(a): the powers or duties of the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(2)(b): the powers or duties of the trustee or other director.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(3): A trustee that acts in reliance on information provided by a trust director is not liable for a breach of trust to the extent the breach resulted from the reliance, unless, by acting, the trustee engages in willful misconduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-110(4): A trust director that acts in reliance on information provided by a trustee or another trust director is not liable for a breach of trust to the extent the breach resulted from the reliance, unless, by acting, the trust director engages in willful misconduct.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111 No duty to monitor, inform, or advise.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(1): (1)(a); (1)(a) Unless the terms of a trust provide otherwise:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(1)(a): a trustee does not have a duty to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(1)(a)(i): monitor a trust director; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(1)(a)(ii): inform or give advice to a settlor, beneficiary, trustee, or trust director concerning an instance in which the trustee might have acted differently than the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(1)(b): (1)(a); (1)(a) by taking an action described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(2): (1)(a); (1)(a) Unless the terms of a trust provide otherwise:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(2)(a): a trust director does not have a duty to:
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(2)(a)(i): monitor a trustee or another trust director; or
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(2)(a)(ii): inform or give advice to a settlor, beneficiary, trustee, or another trust director concerning an instance in which the director might have acted differently than a trustee or another trust director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-111(2)(b): (1)(a); (1)(a) by taking an action described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-112 Application to cotrustee.
---------------------------------------------------------
The terms of a trust may relieve a cotrustee from duty and liability with respect to another cotrustee's exercise or nonexercise of a power of the other cotrustee to the same extent that, in a directed trust, a directed trustee is relieved from duty and liability with respect to a trust director's power of direction under Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-113 Limitation of action against trust director.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-113(1): 75-7-1005 An action against a trust director for a breach of trust must be commenced within the same limitation period as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-113(2): 75-7-1005 A report or accounting has the same effect on the limitation period for an action against a trust director for breach of trust that the report or accounting would have as described in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-114 Defenses in action against trust director.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
In an action against a trust director for a breach of trust, the director may assert the same defenses a trustee in a like position and under similar circumstances could assert in an action for a breach of trust against the trustee.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-115 Jurisdiction over trust director.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-115(1): By accepting appointment as a trust director of a trust subject to this chapter, the director submits to personal jurisdiction of the courts of this state regarding any matter related to a power or duty of the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-115(2): This section does not preclude other methods of obtaining jurisdiction over a trust director.


Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-116 Office of trust director.
---------------------------------------------------------
Unless the terms of a trust provide otherwise, the rules applicable to a trustee apply to a trust director regarding the following matters:Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-116(1): 75-7-701 acceptance under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-116(2): 75-7-702 giving of bond to secure performance under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-116(3): 75-7-708 reasonable compensation under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-116(4): 75-7-705 resignation under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-117 Uniformity of application and construction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
In applying and construing this chapter, consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.

Utah Code Annotated § 75-12-118 Electronic records and signatures.
------------------------------------------------------------------
This chapter modifies, limits, or supersedes the Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001 et seq., but does not modify, limit, or supersede Section 101(c) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices described in Section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. Sec. 7003(b).
